## Agent 1: Research Report: Custom Hooks Library Competitiveness

*Source: a06e6340ce70d8fdf.output*

I'll research popular React hooks libraries to compare with your custom hooks offering.
## Research Report: Custom Hooks Library Competitiveness

**Summary:** Your 10-hook library is largely redundant with mature, free alternatives. Most of your hooks are commodity utilities, though a few may offer value through streamlined APIs or opinionated defaults.

### Competing Libraries Overview

**Mantine Hooks** (~50+ hooks): Industry-standard, zero-dependency library covering state management, performance, browser APIs, and event handling. [Learn more](https://mantine.dev/hooks/)

**usehooks-ts** (~40+ hooks): Minimalist, TypeScript-first, fully tree-shakable library focused on common use cases. [Learn more](https://usehooks-ts.com/)

**react-use** (~70+ hooks): The most comprehensive offering—covers sensors, UI, state, effects, and lifecycle management. [Learn more](https://github.com/streamich/react-use)

**ReactUse** (~110+ hooks): Newest entrant, browser API focus, SSR-compatible. [Learn more](https://reactuse.com/)

### Your Hooks vs. Available Alternatives

**Commodity hooks (easily replaceable):**
- useLocalStorage - available in all three libraries
- useCopyToClipboard - available in Mantine, usehooks-ts, react-use
- useDebounce - available in Mantine (as useDebouncedValue), usehooks-ts
- useTheme - available in all libraries
- useLockBodyScroll - available in react-use

**Partially covered:**
- useScrollProgress - not standard (react-use has useScroll but not progress variant)
- useKeyboardShortcut - partial coverage; libraries have useKey/useHotkey but limited
- useReducedMotion - available in react-use

**Most generic:**
- useMediaQuery - available in all libraries
- useIntersectionObserver - available in react-use, Mantine

### Key Findings

1. **Zero novel hooks**: Every hook you offer exists in at least one mature library
2. **Redundancy rate: 100%**: All 10 are either direct matches or minor variations on commodity utilities
3. **Library ecosystem maturity**: 2025 has dominant, well-maintained, production-ready alternatives (50+ hooks minimum across competitors)
4. **Bundle cost**: You're asking users to add dependencies when existing bundles (react-use ~15KB gzipped) cover all needs

### Recommendation

**Shipping custom hooks is not worthwhile** when users can adopt react-use, usehooks-ts, or Mantine hooks directly. Your value proposition exists only if you offer:
- Tighter integration with your platform (domain-specific workflows)
- Opinionated design patterns your users need
- Composability features unavailable elsewhere

Standard utility hooks belong in established libraries, not custom distributions.

---

**Sources:**
- [Mantine hooks](https://mantine.dev/hooks/)
- [usehooks-ts docs](https://usehooks-ts.com/)
- [react-use GitHub](https://github.com/streamich/react-use)
- [Best React Hooks 2025 comparison](https://digitalthriveai.com/en-gb/resources/web-development/comparing-top-react-hooks-libraries/)
- [Custom hooks decision guide](https://thoughtbot.com/blog/custom-react-hooks)

## Agent 2: Conversion Copywriting Research Report

*Source: a089a9ffba9c4f430.output*

I'll search for professional conversion copywriting research methods and voice of customer mining techniques.
## Conversion Copywriting Research Report

Professional copywriters use a multi-source approach to uncover authentic customer language before writing conversion copy. The gold standard involves combining surveys, interviews, review mining, and social listening to capture the exact words customers use to describe their problems, desires, and solutions.

### Core Research Techniques

**Review Mining** is the most scalable method. Copywriters analyze customer testimonials on Amazon, Google, and industry-specific review sites to extract pain points, objections, and compelling language. The process involves identifying patterns, categorizing feedback into pain points/goals/concerns, and noting specific phrases that resonate.

**Customer Interviews** remain the highest-quality source for discovering emotional drivers and thought processes. One-on-one conversations with customers (current, past, and prospects) reveal the "before state" and "dream state" messaging opportunities.

**Strategic Surveys** capture Voice of Customer data efficiently. High-performing copywriters use single-question surveys at critical moments (post-purchase, post-opt-in) and ask open-ended questions like "What word would you use to describe this program?" to get authentic adjectives and concrete language.

**Social Listening** and comment mining across Reddit, YouTube, support tickets, and public forums reveal unprompted customer concerns and how they naturally discuss problems.

### Message Mining Framework

The extraction process involves:
1. Systematically collecting reviews and interviews
2. Filtering for relevance to your product
3. Segmenting by themes (pain, goals, objections)
4. Extracting exact phrases and language patterns
5. Using these words in headlines, value propositions, and CTAs

The most effective copy mirrors customer language because it creates authenticity—when readers see their own words reflected back, conversion rates increase.

### Sources
- [CopyHackers: 7 Copywriting Research Techniques](https://copyhackers.com/2022/06/copywriting-research/)
- [CXL: Voice of Customer Research](https://cxl.com/blog/voice-of-customer/)
- [Wynter: Copywriting Research Questions](https://wynter.com/post/copywriting-research)
- [HubCopy: Best VoC Research Techniques](https://hubcopy.com/copywriting-research/)
- [Unfold the Story: VoC Data in 2025](https://unfoldthestory.com/strategy/voice-of-customer-data/)

## Agent 3: SaaS Website Narrative Patterns Report

*Source: a0a6532adf3863f8c.output*

I'll search for current SaaS website narrative patterns and analyze how leading companies structure their messaging.
## SaaS Website Narrative Patterns Report

**Dominant Homepage Structure (2026)**

Leading SaaS sites follow this sequence: Hero (8-12 word value prop) → Social proof (logos/metrics top-placed, not buried) → Problem/Solution narrative → Product in context (screenshots, interactive demos) → Case studies (Challenge-Solution-Impact framework) → Clear CTA.

**Recurring Copy Patterns**

- **Hero clarity**: Answer "What does this do?" and "Is it for me?" in 3-5 seconds
- **Customer as hero**: Position prospect as protagonist, company as mentor, problem as antagonist (22x better recall vs. feature lists)
- **Staged proof**: Layer testimonials by decision stage (orientation → credibility → effort → commitment), not clustered
- **Friction removal**: Progressive profiling, sticky CTAs, no pricing gatekeeping

**Company Playbooks**

- **Stripe**: Gradient animations + statistics + recognizable logos = technical sophistication + credibility
- **Notion**: Templates + realistic use cases + warm illustrations = eliminates feature confusion
- **Linear**: Real interface screenshots integrated = transparency + authentic product preview
- **Vercel**: Fast demos + developer-focused proof points

**Conversion Science**

5-8 sections optimal. Single primary CTA repeated. Social proof lifts conversions 37% average (10-270% range). Section order matters: orientation → confidence → effort evaluation → commitment. Skip a stage, visitors shop elsewhere.

**Key Insight**: Successful sites copy structure/logic/flow, not visuals. Whitespace-rich design. Product displayed directly. Page speed: each second = 7% conversion drop.

---

- [B2B Storytelling Narrative](https://www.fletchpmm.com/resource/5-narrative-structures-for-b2b-messaging)

## Agent 4: Lenis Smooth Scroll: 2026 Status Report

*Source: a0e50829c9b2df033.output*

I'll search for the current status of Lenis smooth scroll in 2026.
## Lenis Smooth Scroll: 2026 Status Report

**Latest Version:** v1.3.21 (released March 26, 2026)
- Recent updates focus on scroll-margin/scroll-padding fixes and issue resolution
- Sub-4KB library, actively maintained with regular releases

**Industry Standing:** Still dominant
- Lightweight (2.13KB core), accessible, plays well with ScrollTrigger
- Preferred for native DOM structures and vanilla scroll control
- Used by top agencies and developers worldwide

**Competitors & Alternatives:**
- **GSAP ScrollSmoother**: Powerful but rigid; better for animation-heavy sites
- **Locomotive Scroll**: Lost market share significantly since Lenis emerged
- **Vanilla JS**: Growing trend toward pure JS scroll listeners + CSS transforms

**Breaking Changes:** None reported in recent releases; focus on refinements

**Verdict:** Lenis remains the industry standard for smooth scrolling in 2026. No major challengers, though vanilla JS minimalism is gaining adoption for simple use cases.

- [Lenis Official](https://www.lenis.dev/)
- [GitHub Releases](https://github.com/darkroomengineering/lenis/releases)

## Agent 5: Data Storytelling on the Web: Essential Rules & Approaches

*Source: a10c9bc44895884a8.output*

I'll search for current best practices on data storytelling on the web in 2026.
## Data Storytelling on the Web: Essential Rules & Approaches

**Core Framework**
Data storytelling combines three elements: accurate data, narrative arc (problem → insight → solution), and visual representation. The most effective approach begins with **specific data points**, not abstractions. [The Pudding's method](https://www.storybench.org/pudding-structures-stories-visual-essays/) exemplifies this: start with a single character or statistic (e.g., "truck drivers") before scaling to broader insights.

**Statistics as Proof Points**
- **Specific > Abstract**: "79% of readers scan vs. read fully" beats "most people skim"
- **Relative > Absolute**: Percentages and comparisons land harder than raw numbers
- **Personal > Aggregate**: Begin with individual data points; contextualize with larger trends

[Proof points require verification](https://buildingmomentum.io/proof-points-in-marketing/)—accuracy builds lasting credibility.

**Data Visualization as Narrative Climax**
Visual essays work best with sparse text where design and data carry the story. [Narrative visualization structures](http://vis.stanford.edu/files/2010-Narrative-InfoVis.pdf) include:
- **Martini Glass**: Author-driven overview → reader-driven exploration
- **Annotated visuals**: Guide audiences to key takeaways
- **Rhythm**: Vary intensity to maintain engagement

**2026 Trends**
[Narrative dashboards](https://infogram.com/blog/10-trends-in-data-visualization-to-watch-in-2026/) now combine interactive elements with structured storytelling. [Narrative arbitrage](https://www.influencers-time.com/uncovering-narrative-arbitrage-hidden-stories-in-data-2026/)—surfacing overlooked insights—differentiates brands.

**Design Process** (The Pudding approach)
Think backwards from takeaway: What do readers need to understand? Ruthless editing ensures every element advances the story.

Sources: [Storytelling with Data](https://www.storytellingwithdata.com/), [ThoughtSpot](https://www.thoughtspot.com/data-trends/best-practices/data-storytelling), [The Pudding](https://pudding.cool/)

## Agent 6: Multi-Agent Token Cost Optimization Report

*Source: a110fc632ee2fd623.output*

I'll search for current information on multi-agent token cost optimization patterns in 2026.
## Multi-Agent Token Cost Optimization Report

**Cost Crisis Context:** Agents make 3-10x more LLM calls than chatbots. A single unconstrained engineering task costs $5-8 in API fees; comprehensive optimization reduces costs 70-90%.

**Key Strategies:**

1. **Prompt Caching** — The highest-ROI technique. Reuses computed attention tensors for repeated system prompts and tool definitions across dozens of calls. Caching eliminates 40-90% of redundant computation; cached tokens cost 75-90% less depending on provider (Anthropic: 90%, OpenAI: 50%).

2. **Model Routing** — Route tasks to appropriate model size. Frontier models for complex reasoning, cheap models for classification/extraction. The "frontier orchestrator + cheap sub-agents" pattern cuts costs 40-60% without quality loss.

3. **Semantic Caching** — Cache responses by query embeddings, not exact string matching. Multiple agents requesting same data retrieve cached results.

4. **Smart Context Handoffs** — Pass only relevant data between agents (500 tokens vs 5,000-20,000 for full conversation history). Avoid chatty agents over-communicating unnecessary details.

5. **Structured Orchestration** — Code-driven orchestration is more deterministic than LLM-controlled; combined with supervised/adaptive patterns reduces variance by 200%+ vs custom approaches.

**Real-World Results:** 20-40% cost reductions with 25-60% efficiency gains; combined techniques achieve 60-80% savings.

**When to Use Each Model:**
- Frontier (Claude 3.5 Sonnet, GPT-4o): orchestration, complex reasoning
- Mid-tier (Claude 3 Haiku, GPT-4o Mini): task execution, routing decisions
- Cheap (local/open models): classification, extraction, formatting

**Sources:**
- [Cost Optimization Guide 2026](https://moltbook-ai.com/posts/ai-agent-cost-optimization-2026)
- [Reducing Costs 90%](https://medium.com/@ravityuval/how-i-reduced-llm-token-costs-by-90-using-prompt-rag-and-ai-agent-optimization-f64bd1b56d9f)
- [Token Optimization Speed & Cost](https://redis.io/blog/llm-token-optimization-speed-up-apps/)
- [Cost Per Token 2026 Guide](https://www.silicondata.com/blog/llm-cost-per-token)
- [Multi-Agent Orchestration Overview](https://www.talkdesk.com/blog/multi-agent-orchestration/)
- [Azure Agent Design Patterns](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/architecture/ai-ml/guide/ai-agent-design-patterns)
- [AI Cost Crisis & DePIN Solutions](https://www.financialcontent.com/article/abnewswire-2026-3-30-the-2026-ai-cost-crisis-how-aiccs-one-api-powers-agentic-ai-with-unified-access-superior-data-and-decentralized-compute)

## Agent 7: E-Commerce Product Storytelling Report

*Source: a11d58ad3099ef16b.output*

I'll search for e-commerce product storytelling practices and DTC brand narrative strategies.
## E-Commerce Product Storytelling Report

**How DTC/E-Commerce Brands Tell Product Stories:**

DTC brands prioritize authentic narratives showing brand purpose over product features. A proven structure uses the customer as hero, their problem as villain, and the brand as guide. Storytelling creates 65% better information retention versus plain facts and builds emotional trust that reduces purchase objections. Sensory language—describing product experience rather than specs—bridges the online-to-reality gap that makes physical retail compelling.

**Page-Level Narrative Differences:**

- **Product Pages** emphasize emotive storytelling and benefit-driven copy with sensory details. They connect product features to customer psychology and pain points, creating personal emotional resonance.
- **Category Pages** balance commercial intent with informational content (300-450 words). They guide shoppers through product groupings and account for 60% of organic traffic, requiring keyword optimization without sacrificing image-focused design.
- **Brand Pages** establish core values, mission, and company vision—the foundational story that all product narratives reinforce.

**What's Different from SaaS:**

E-commerce storytelling emphasizes immediate sensory experience and emotional connection (how the product *feels*), while SaaS focuses on workflow efficiency and business outcomes. E-commerce uses shorter narratives across multiple touchpoints (product, category, email, ads); SaaS builds longer-form thought leadership. DTC brands treat websites as "global flagship stores"—cohesive content-commerce fusion—whereas SaaS prioritizes free-trial conversion and ROI messaging.

## Agent 11: Nonprofit Website Storytelling: Structure & Donor Psychology

*Source: a1aab98e60d87f979.output*

I'll search for comprehensive information on nonprofit website storytelling for you.
## Nonprofit Website Storytelling: Structure & Donor Psychology

**Narrative Architecture:**
Effective nonprofit sites use three-act structure: Connection (emotional hook through shared values), Rising Action (sensory details building tension), and Resolution (hope-infused impact). Stories are 22x more memorable than facts; 92% of consumers prefer advertising in story form.

**Donor Psychology Drivers:**
Key triggers include Empathy (connecting with individuals), Urgency (time-sensitive impact), Trust (wise resource use), and Social Proof (donor community). Counter-intuitively, adding 500% more copy to donation pages increases conversions—not less. Optimal pages use 3-4 default donation amounts plus custom options.

**Urgency vs. Hope Tension:**
The critical balance: hook with anecdotal conflict/urgency, then spend more time on resolution (the turning point where support creates change) than hardship. Effective copy articulates "why give now?" through statistics and impact testimonies. Avoid overwhelming audiences by balancing honesty about problems with hope about solutions.

**Web Narrative Strategy:**
Position a specific character (not vague groups) as the emotional center. Use all five senses to immerse readers. Share metrics *after* emotional narrative hooks readers. Include small details that maintain investment while tension builds toward a call to action.

**Sources:**
- [Instrumentl: Nonprofit Storytelling Tips](https://www.instrumentl.com/blog/storytelling-for-nonprofits-tips)
- [The Storytelling Nonprofit: Story Structure](https://www.thestorytellingnonprofit.com/blog/storystructure/)
- [Sure Impact: Impact Story Toolkit](https://www.sureimpact.com/post/impact-story)
- [Charity CFO: Psychology of Fundraising](https://thecharitycfo.com/the-psychology-of-fundraising-why-do-donors-give/)
- [NextAfter: Best Donation Page Setup 2024](https://www.nextafter.com/blog/donation-pages/)
- [Keela: Power of Nonprofit Storytelling](https://www.keela.co/blog/nonprofit-resources/nonprofit-storytelling)
- [Amy Eisenstein: 3-Act Structure for Fundraisers](https://www.amyeisenstein.com/storytelling-for-nonprofit-fundraisers-3-acts/)

## Mission 21 — Gestalt Principles in Digital Design

**Findings:**

The core Gestalt canon (proximity, continuity, closure, similarity, common region, figure/ground, symmetry, and now synchrony/common fate) remains stable with no new principles emerging in 2026. The notable evolution is in _application context_:

- **Pre-attentive processing in scrolling:** 2025 CHI research confirms scroll immersion disrupts working memory and produces cognitive fatigue — the very attentional budget the synthesis document already models. The implication for web-god: scroll scenes that violate pre-attentive rules (too many competing salience channels) compound fatigue effects measured in lab settings. The 200–250ms pre-attentive window remains the gold standard citation.
- **Von Restorff / Isolation Effect:** No new empirical updates found for 2025–2026. The principle is stable: one primary isolation per scene (STAR moment), overuse collapses hierarchy. Current practice focuses on applying it to pricing tiers, primary CTAs, and cinematic transition moments — exactly what synthesis.md already codifies.
- **AI-generated layouts:** The emerging angle is that AI design tools (Figma AI, v0, Galileo) are being evaluated on Gestalt coherence as an automated layout quality signal. This is new territory: Gestalt as a _machine-readable_ quality metric, not just a designer heuristic.
- **WCAG 2.2 intersection:** Accessibility mandates are pushing proximity and contrast principles to become compliance requirements, not just aesthetic choices.

**Sources:**
- [IxDF Gestalt Principles 2026](https://ixdf.org/literature/topics/gestalt-principles)
- [Clay: Gestalt Design Principles](https://clay.global/blog/gestalt-design-principles)
- [ScienceDirect: Scroll Immersion & Cognitive Fatigue (2025)](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0001691825009874)
- [CHI 2025: Scrolling & Attention Interventions](https://dl.acm.org/doi/10.1145/3706598.3713187)

## Mission 22 — Core Web Vitals Evolution

**Findings:**

Two new metrics have entered the ecosystem in 2026:

1. **Visual Stability Index (VSI):** Session-scoped replacement/companion to CLS. CLS measures shifts at page load; VSI measures layout stability across the entire user session — including shifts during scrolling, interactions, and SPA route changes. This directly hits scroll-driven sites that mutate layout mid-session. No confirmed "good/needs improvement/poor" thresholds found yet — still in rollout.

2. **Engagement Reliability (ER):** Measures consistency of interactions across all session touchpoints — buttons that fail, forms that stall, interactions that produce no visible response. Distinct from INP (which measures latency of individual interactions) in that ER tracks _failure rate across the session_, not per-interaction speed.

**Existing metric updates:**
- LCP threshold: still ≤2.5s (unchanged)
- INP threshold: ≤200ms good / 200–500ms needs improvement / >500ms poor (unchanged from March 2024 launch, but enforcement weight increased)
- CLS threshold: ≤0.1 (unchanged)
- **Critical 2026 ranking change:** Core Web Vitals have shifted from a tiebreaker to a _filter_ — the March 10, 2026 core update means red CWV scores can suppress well-ranked content. 43% of sites currently fail the 200ms INP threshold.
- Mobile CWV scores now carry increased weight in overall ranking signals.

**INP optimization stack confirmed for 2026:**
- React: `useDeferredValue`, `useTransition`, `React.memo`
- General: Web Workers for processing, `content-visibility: auto`, CSS containment, list virtualization, `@defer` (Angular)

**Sources:**
- [SEOlogist: CWV Key Updates 2026](https://www.seologist.com/knowledge-sharing/core-web-vitals-whats-changed/)
- [Mewa Studio: SEO & CWV 2026](https://www.mewastudio.com/en/blog/seo-core-web-vitals-2026)
- [ALM Corp: CWV Technical SEO 2026](https://almcorp.com/blog/core-web-vitals-2026-technical-seo-guide/)
- [NitroPack: Most Important CWV Metrics 2026](https://nitropack.io/blog/most-important-core-web-vitals-metrics/)
- [Koanthic: CWV 2026 Complete INP Guide](https://koanthic.com/en/core-web-vitals-2026-complete-inp-guide-assessment/)
- [LinkGraph: INP Optimization 2026](https://www.linkgraph.com/blog/interaction-to-next-paint-optimization/)
- [Eiysys: Next-Gen CWV](https://www.eiysys.com/blog/next-gen-core-web-vitals-new-performance/)

**Relevance to web-god:** Critical for `agents/performance/auditor.md`, `agents/seo/auditor.md`, and `skills/performance/`. VSI is a direct threat to scroll-driven sites — any scrollytelling output that mutates layout mid-scroll will register VSI shifts. ER affects any interactive component in the stack.

**Action:** Update `agents/performance/auditor.md` to audit for VSI and ER in addition to the existing LCP/INP/CLS checks. Add VSI-specific guidance to `agents/scrollytelling/` agents (director/choreographer) about avoiding layout-shifting scroll effects. Update `agents/seo/auditor.md` to reflect the CWV-as-filter ranking change and the increased mobile weight. Priority: **P0**, Effort: **M**

## Mission 23 — Doherty Threshold & Perceived Performance

**Findings:**

The Doherty Threshold (sub-400ms system response for flow state) itself has no new empirical updates — the 1982 IBM research remains the canonical citation. What has evolved is its relationship to modern measurement standards:

- **INP ≤200ms as the new de facto target:** Google's INP "good" threshold (200ms at 75th percentile) is now stricter than the Doherty Threshold. Hitting INP automatically satisfies Doherty for discrete interactions. This means web-god's performance budgeting can unify around 200ms for interaction responsiveness, dropping the legacy 400ms framing.
- **120Hz / variable refresh rate:** ProMotion-like variable refresh rate displays are now mainstream across mobile (iOS, Android 15 ARR) and desktop (Apple Studio Display XDR at 120Hz announced March 2026). The implication: `requestAnimationFrame` callbacks fire at 120fps on these devices. Scroll animations capped at 60fps logic will run correctly but won't leverage the additional smoothness budget. GSAP and CSS scroll-driven animations both honor the display's native refresh rate. The browser constraint (battery, thermal) still gates 120fps in practice — but high-priority animations on flagship hardware will run there.
- **No new "120fps threshold" research found.** The perceptual advantage of 120fps over 60fps for scroll animations remains an open UX research question — no 2025–2026 study was surfaced. The practical guidance from the Android ARR documentation is that `requestAnimationFrame` dynamically matches content render rate when ARR is enabled.
- **Perceived performance toolkit is stable:** Skeleton screens, optimistic UI, progress indicators, and animation-as-feedback remain the canonical tools for the sub-400ms illusion. No new pattern has emerged.

**Sources:**
- [Laws of UX: Doherty Threshold](https://lawsofux.com/doherty-threshold/)
- [LogRocket: Designing for Instant Feedback (Doherty)](https://blog.logrocket.com/ux-design/designing-instant-feedback-doherty-threshold/)
- [UXGen Studio: Doherty Threshold](https://uxgenstudio.com/ux-laws/the-doherty-threshold/)
- [TechTimes: 120Hz ProMotion Displays 2026](https://www.techtimes.com/articles/314590/20260213/how-120hz-promotionlike-displays-actually-improve-scrolling-smoothness-battery-life.htm)
- [Apple: Studio Display XDR 120Hz (March 2026)](https://www.apple.com/newsroom/2026/03/apple-unveils-new-studio-display-and-all-new-studio-display-xdr/)
- [Android: Adaptive Refresh Rate (ARR)](https://developer.android.com/develop/ui/views/animations/adaptive-refresh-rate)
- [NitroPack: INP Optimization](https://nitropack.io/blog/interaction-to-next-paint-inp/)

**Relevance to web-god:** The 200ms INP target superseding 400ms Doherty needs to be reflected in `agents/performance/profiler.md` and `research/synthesis.md`. The 120Hz mainstreaming is relevant to `agents/scrollytelling/choreographer.md` — animations should not artificially cap at 60fps when the platform supports higher.

**Action:** Update `research/synthesis.md` to note that INP ≤200ms is now the operative performance floor for interactions (stricter than Doherty's 400ms). Add a note to `agents/scrollytelling/choreographer.md` that GSAP and CSS scroll-driven animations should not cap `requestAnimationFrame` logic — let the browser match the display refresh rate. Priority: **P1**, Effort: **S**

## Mission 24 — Cinematic Web Design Trends

**Findings:**

This is the highest-signal mission for the scrollytelling domain. Key confirmed 2026 trends:

- **Scroll-driven storytelling is the dominant premium technique.** Awwwards showcases and trend roundups from Webflow, Codrops, and UX Pilot all converge: scroll-driven narrative with GSAP + CSS scroll-driven animations + WebGL (Three.js/OGL) is the current gold standard for award-winning sites.
- **Specific Codrops tutorials published in 2026:** "Building a Scroll-Revealed WebGL Gallery with GSAP, Three.js, Astro and Barba.js" (Feb 2, 2026) and "Sticky Grid Scroll: Building a Scroll-Driven Animated Grid" (March 2, 2026) — confirming active production of this pattern at the craft level.
- **Inkwell (Awwwards-featured):** A scroll-driven narrative site for an AI company. Built with Vue.js + OGL (WebGL) + RapierJS (physics). Treatment was filmic: the concepting phase was run as film pre-production — storyboards for scroll triggers, pacing plotted as a timeline rather than wireframes. This is identical to the auteur methodology in `research/synthesis.md`.
- **Particle/WebGL physics:** Three.js deconstruction of 2D images into 3D particle matrices with physics-based explosion effects on scroll transitions is a confirmed Awwwards-award pattern.
- **Imperfect by Design (Canva 2026 trend report):** A counter-trend to hyper-polished digital. Intentional grain, texture, noise, and "organic imperfection" signals are appearing as an aesthetic response to AI-generated smoothness. This is not anti-cinematic — it is _analog cinematic_ (film grain, vignetting, hand-drawn elements).
- **Oversized kinetic typography over full-screen video** remains a dominant hero section pattern.
- **Horizontal scroll / timeline navigation** is gaining as a structural pattern for chapter-based narratives.
- **Parallax is still alive:** Confirmed still relevant in 2026 but must be implemented with VRR-awareness and scroll-fatigue mitigation (scene boundaries, pause moments).

**Sources:**

## Agent 15: Narrative Brief Research: Key Findings

*Source: a227b7a0b2b4974b6.output*

I'll search for current narrative brief templates and best practices to understand what makes a good narrative brief.
## Narrative Brief Research: Key Findings

**What Makes a Good Narrative Brief?**

A narrative brief combines storytelling with strategic direction. Unlike traditional design briefs (specification-focused), narrative briefs use anecdotes, user scenarios, mood boards, and character perspectives to bring context to life. [Metropolis Magazine](https://metropolismag.com/viewpoints/using-narratives-for-design-briefings/) emphasizes that narratives "instruct and inspire"—they increase the likelihood the brief will actually be read and understood.

**Essential Inputs for Narrative Strategists:**

- Brand narrative & core messages (unique value propositions)
- Target audience psychographics (pain points, motivations, desires)
- Brand voice/tone specifications
- Project overview & deliverables
- Success metrics & business objectives

[Big Bang Copy](https://www.bigbangcopy.com/blog/copywriting-brief-template) and [Asana](https://asana.com/resources/how-write-creative-brief-examples-template) both stress that copywriting briefs need deep audience insight beyond demographics.

**Design Brief vs. Narrative Brief:**

Design briefs are dry, specification-heavy documents with tables and bullet points. Narrative briefs embed those specs within storytelling—user scenarios, character journeys, metaphors—making strategic intent tangible and memorable. [Architecture Narratives article](https://www.archisoup.com/studio-guide/architecture-narratives) shows how this approach helps designers "put themselves in users' shoes."

**Can They Combine?**

Yes. Modern creative briefs integrate both approaches. [Monday.com (2026)](https://monday.com/blog/project-management/creative-brief-template/) shows that 2026 briefs emphasize "context"—pulling insights from past campaigns, analyzing performance, and embedding narrative into actionable workflows. The winning formula: narrative framing with specifications embedded naturally within user-centered stories.

**Sources:**
- [Monday.com Creative Brief 2026](https://monday.com/blog/project-management/creative-brief-template/)
- [Metropolis: Narratives for Design](https://metropolismag.com/viewpoints/using-narratives-for-design-briefings/)
- [Big Bang Copy Template](https://www.bigbangcopy.com/blog/copywriting-brief-template)
- [Canva Creative Briefs Guide](https://www.canva.com/docs/creative-briefs/)

## Agent 16: Research Update: Attention Economics & Cognitive Load (March 2026)

*Source: a22cdf8c0f4d59151.output*

I'll search for the latest research on attention economics and cognitive load in web design.
## Research Update: Attention Economics & Cognitive Load (March 2026)

**Key Findings:**

**50 Bits/Second Bottleneck:** The classical 50 bits/second consciousness bandwidth (from 1940s neuroscience) remains foundational but rarely updated. Recent work (2025) discusses the lower figure of ~10 bits/s for actual information throughput. No major challenge to the model—rather, refinement toward more precise measurement of conscious attention capacity.

**2026 Design Response:** Rather than challenging the bottleneck, designers are *designing around* it. The emphasis shifted from 2025 (adding flair) to 2026 (stripping waste). Key tactics: brevity as respect for attention, text effects signaling importance, performance-first design, and cognitive ease through clarity and reduced distractions.

**New Cognitive Load Models:** 2024-2026 research moves beyond theory to measurement systems using eye-tracking, task completion time, and error rates. Emerging focus on:
- Elderly user cognitive load in mobile interfaces
- Real-time dynamic assessment via algorithmic strain detection
- Interface complexity effects on task interruption scenarios
- Accessibility-integrated cognitive load reduction

**Bottom Line:** The 50 bits/second constraint isn't being overturned—it's being operationalized. Web design now treats attention scarcity as a first-class design problem with measurable, data-driven optimization strategies.

## Agent 17: Core Web Vitals 2026 Update Summary

## Core Web Vitals 2026 Update Summary

**Key Changes:**
- **New Metric:** Visual Stability Index (VSI) introduced—smarter CLS that ignores anticipated layout shifts (e.g., user-triggered dropdowns) but penalizes unexpected ones
- **INP Elevation:** Interaction to Next Paint formalized as primary ranking signal (equal weight to LCP/CLS)
- **INP Thresholds Tightened:** "Good" now 150ms (down from 200ms); "needs improvement" 150-500ms; "poor" 500ms+
- **LCP Threshold Tightened:** 2.0 seconds (down from 2.5s per some sources)
- **CLS:** Remains under 0.1
- **Ranking Impact:** March 2026 core update strengthened performance weight significantly; INP violations cause 0.8-4 position drops

**New Ranking Signals (2026):**
- Content originality & first-hand experience over rephrasing
- Topical authority & E-E-A-T
- User engagement (scroll depth, time on page, repeat visits)
- Mobile-first performance emphasis

## Agent 18: Emerging Interaction Paradigms Beyond Scroll (March 2026)

*Source: a2977c3fe82944c95.output*

## Emerging Interaction Paradigms Beyond Scroll (March 2026)

Four major paradigms are reshaping web interaction:

**Spatial Computing:** WebXR standards mature in 2026—Safari enables spatial browsing with inline 3D models via HTML `<model>` element and immersive video support. Snap's Consumer Spectacles launch with native browser and WebXR, reaching enterprise ($182B→$221B market).

**Vision-Native Experiences:** Apple visionOS 26 brings Reader mode spatial scenes and CSS-styleable 3D objects directly to web pages, transforming articles and retail experiences without native app requirements.

**Gesture Navigation:** Air-swiping, eye-tracking selection, and motion sensors replace scroll as web input methods. Emerging "experimental navigation" uses AI-adaptive gesture recognition for accessibility breakthroughs.

**Haptic Feedback:** Vibration API extends web responsiveness—tactile confirmation improves task speed (+35%), retention (+23%), satisfaction (+27%). Forms, navigation, and e-commerce adopt haptic layers.

**Moonshot:** Voice-driven scrollytelling (voice narration + spatial pacing), eye-gaze pagination, and distributed haptic networks create genuinely alien browsing experiences vs. 2010s paradigms.

## Edge Computing Deployment Report (March 2026)

### Key Patterns & Technologies

**Latest Edge Platforms:**
- [Vercel Edge Functions](https://vercel.com/docs/functions/runtimes/edge/edge-functions.rsc): Now integrated into Vercel Functions with Edge Runtime. Supports streaming, no max duration (must respond in 25s). [Edge Config](https://vercel.com/docs/edge-config) enables feature flags and A/B testing at edge.
- [Cloudflare Workers 2026](https://developers.cloudflare.com/changelog/): Dynamic Workers (open beta) spin up workers at runtime. New mTLS support, Python Workflows support, and [Containers/Sandboxes outbound connectivity](https://developers.cloudflare.com/changelog/post/2026-03-26-outbound-workers/).

**Dominant Pattern:**
Run authentication, routing, and personalization at edge while keeping app servers/databases centralized. Reduces TTFB by 60-80%, collapses latency from 150-300ms to under 50ms.

**Emerging Tech:**
WebAssembly at the edge enables Rust, Go, C++, Python for edge logic with near-native speed—critical for complex computations beyond JavaScript.

**DevOps Should Know:**
- Edge as baseline for global TTFB <50ms (Vercel, Cloudflare, Fly.io, Netlify)
- Edge databases (distributed state): R2, KV stores for fast regional access
- Middleware layers at edge for auth/routing before origin
- Active CPU pricing models across platforms

## Agent 20: Frame Rate Perception Research Report (2026)

*Source: a2e53c35de6d70d60.output*

I'll search for current information on frame rate perception and web animation in 2026.
## Frame Rate Perception Research Report (2026)

### 120fps vs 60fps: Current Target
**120fps is now the target.** Major brands (Spotify, Duolingo, Disney, Google) actively deploy 120fps animations using Rive's GPU-accelerated engine. However, browser support remains inconsistent: CSS animations run at 120Hz+ on 120Hz+ devices, while JS-driven `requestAnimationFrame` is still capped at 60fps. Apple throttles higher rates by default for battery efficiency.

### Doherty Threshold (400ms Rule)
The Doherty Threshold remains foundational: users perceive systems as responsive when interaction latency stays under 400ms. Modern approaches use perceived performance techniques—skeleton screens, progress bars, animations—to mask longer processes, making systems *feel* faster even when actual response time exceeds the threshold.

### Variable Refresh Rate (VRR)
**VRR support in browsers is minimal.** W3C proposals (GitHub issue #375) push for VSYNC OFF and VRR control exposure to web apps, but no mainstream browser currently implements it. VRR could eliminate screen tearing by syncing refresh rates to fixed frame rates (24, 30, 60 fps), but browser-level adoption remains theoretical.

### Key Takeaway
Expectations have shifted from "good enough at 60fps" to "smooth at 120fps," but infrastructure (browser APIs, battery efficiency, standards) hasn't fully caught up.

**Sources:**
- [Rive Animation Engine](https://rive.app/)
- [Laws of UX: Doherty Threshold](https://lawsofux.com/doherty-threshold/)
- [WICG VRR Proposal](https://github.com/WICG/proposals/issues/208)
- [W3C VSYNC API Issue](https://github.com/w3c/html/issues/375)
- [Blur Busters VRR Research](https://blurbusters.com/adding-variable-refresh-rate-support-to-html-5-2/)

## Agent 22: How People Read on the Web in 2026

*Source: a3290e2e3377ee8c7.output*

I'll research how people read on the web in 2026, focusing on reading patterns and their implications for content structure.
## How People Read on the Web in 2026

Web reading hasn't fundamentally changed since Nielsen Norman's original 2006 research—users still scan rather than read every word (only ~28% of text is processed). Three primary patterns persist:

**F-Pattern & Layer-Cake:** The F-shaped scan (horizontal sweep at top, second shorter sweep mid-page, vertical sweep left edge) remains most effective for text-heavy content. The layer-cake pattern—where eyes fixate on headings/subheadings then drop to relevant body text—is equally viable and often more efficient for finding specific information.

**Z-Pattern Evolution:** Best for CTA-focused, lower-density pages, creating a natural eye flow across key elements.

### What's Changed Since 2006

The core patterns persist, but 2026 design reflects new input contexts:
- **AI-trained expectations:** Feed-style scanning and summaries have conditioned users to expect bite-sized, scannable chunks
- **Mobile-first reality:** F-patterns still apply but tighter columns force earlier vertical scanning
- **Visual hierarchy emphasis:** Bold typography, whitespace, and grid layouts now critical for scannability—dense paragraphs feel heavy
- **Narrative-driven structure:** Hero sections with empty promises are out; pages with clear value hierarchy are in

### Practical Implications

Effective 2026 copy strategy: strong descriptive headings (skip generic titles), chunked paragraphs, bullet lists, and clear visual hierarchy that respects natural scan paths. Layer-cake organization with prominent subheadings outperforms plain text for discoverability. The research confirms scannable design isn't about *writing less*—it's about *structuring more intelligently*.

**Sources:**
- [Nielsen Norman: F-Shaped Pattern](https://www.nngroup.com/articles/f-shaped-pattern-reading-web-content/)
- [Nielsen Norman: Layer-Cake Pattern](https://www.nngroup.com/articles/layer-cake-pattern-scanning/)
- [Nielsen Norman: Text Scanning Patterns](https://www.nngroup.com/articles/text-scanning-patterns-eyetracking/)
- [Nielsen Norman: How People Read on the Web](https://www.nngroup.com/reports/how-people-read-web-eyetracking-evidence/)
- [UXPin: Website Design for Scannability](https://www.uxpin.com/studio/blog/website-design-for-scannability/)

## Mission 37 — No-Code Scrollytelling Tools

**Findings:**

The no-code scrollytelling landscape in 2026 has a clear hierarchy of capability with a hard ceiling. The most significant recent development: **Webflow acquired GSAP in early 2026 and removed its historical freemium paywall entirely**, then integrated full GSAP + ScrollTrigger support directly into its visual builder. This means Webflow users now get near-JavaScript-grade scroll animation power without writing JavaScript — the biggest single shift to the no-code ceiling in years.

**Webflow** is dominant for content-heavy, multi-page sites with complex CMS needs. Its GSAP integration gives it the deepest scroll animation toolkit in the no-code space. **Framer** remains the preferred choice for high-impact visual landing pages — faster to set up, more design-forward, excellent for single-page narratives with scroll-triggered variant changes and sticky text reveals. However, Framer has documented precision limitations: complex multi-step sequences with staggered timing, conditional logic, or element-to-element interactions are difficult to fine-tune.

**The differentiation line:** No-code tools handle single-element triggers, reveals, parallax, and basic scroll-linked transforms extremely well. Where they break down is synchronized multi-actor sequences (e.g. a canvas animation driving a GSAP timeline driving a React state machine), conditional narrative branches, physics-based scroll, and pixel-perfect performance tuning. That gap is where code — specifically GSAP + ScrollTrigger + custom JS — still wins. A Codrops article from January 2026 ("The Spark") explicitly documents how advanced productions still wire GSAP and 3D graphics engines together via JavaScript scroll controllers precisely because no-code tools cannot coordinate across layers at that fidelity.

**Sources:**
- [Webflow scroll animation examples](https://webflow.com/made-in-webflow/scroll-animation)
- [Animate an element while scrolling – Webflow Help Center](https://help.webflow.com/hc/en-us/articles/33961292762771-Animate-an-element-while-scrolling)
- [The Spark: Engineering an Immersive, Story-First Web Experience | Codrops](https://tympanus.net/codrops/2026/01/09/the-spark-engineering-an-immersive-story-first-web-experience/)
- [Framer scroll animations](https://www.framer.com/academy/lessons/scroll-animations)
- [Cool Scrolling Effect Like Apple with Framer (0 code)](https://www.framer.com/blog/cool-scrolling-effect/)
- [Webflow vs Framer 2026: Complete Comparison](https://www.gemeosagency.com/en/blog/webflow-vs-framer-which-no-code-tool-to-choose)
- [Scroll Animation Tools 2026: Which One Should You Actually Use?](https://cssauthor.com/scroll-animation-tools/)
- [Best JavaScript Scroll Animation & Scrollytelling Libraries 2026](https://cssauthor.com/best-javascript-scroll-animation-scrollytelling-libraries/)

**Relevance to web-god:** The `webgod-scrollytelling` skill sits precisely at the differentiation line — it should position itself as what you reach for when no-code tools hit their ceiling. Webflow + GSAP now covers a large swathe of standard scrollytelling; web-god's value is in the sequences no visual tool can express. The skill should also integrate awareness that many users come from Webflow/Framer and need a migration or augmentation path, not a replacement.

**Action:** Update `webgod-scrollytelling` skill documentation and prompting to explicitly address the "I'm using Webflow/Framer — what can't it do?" entry point. Add GSAP-first patterns for multi-actor sequences that no-code tools cannot coordinate. Priority: **P1**, Effort: **S**

## Mission 38 — Developer Experience Trends

**Findings:**

By 2026, roughly **85% of developers regularly use AI tools for coding**. The market has stratified into two distinct archetypes that developers increasingly use in combination:

**Claude Code** is terminal-based, autonomous, and excels at multi-file refactors, test generation, and large-codebase understanding. Benchmarks show 8.5 accuracy points per dollar on complex tasks vs Cursor's 6.2. Its weakness is cost ($100–200/month for Max) and the absence of inline IDE flow.

**Cursor** is IDE-native, excels at Tab autocomplete (widely called the best inline completion available in 2026), rapid JSX iteration, and interactive styling. 42 accuracy points per dollar on simple utility tasks. Costs $20/month.

**The emerging consensus:** power users run both. Claude Code handles autonomous reasoning-heavy execution (architecture, refactors, feature builds); Cursor handles in-the-flow editing. Developers now judge tools on **net productivity across the full workflow** — not isolated moments of assistance. Trust (data privacy, no training on proprietary code), cost-effectiveness, and first-pass correctness are the top evaluation criteria.

**Where skills fit:** Skills in Claude Code's ecosystem are valued as **workflow accelerators for domain-specific tasks** that generic prompting handles poorly — the same way IDE plugins extended editors. Developers want skills that encode expert patterns they would otherwise have to prompt-engineer from scratch on every session. The emerging skill of "writing effective prompts" is itself being professionalized, which signals that well-structured skills with embedded expert context are a genuine DX differentiator.

**Sources:**

**Relevance to web-god:** web-god skills are a direct response to this trend. They embed domain expertise (scrollytelling, performance, security, SEO) that developers otherwise have to reconstruct through prompt engineering. The package's value proposition aligns precisely with what the market is rewarding: first-pass correctness on complex, domain-specific tasks.

**Action:** Craft web-god's README and skill descriptions around the "net productivity" framing — not "Claude can do X" but "web-god gives Claude expert-level domain context so the first pass is production-grade." Explicitly position against the Cursor+Claude Code workflow. Priority: **P1**, Effort: **S**

## Mission 39 — Open Source Monetization

**Findings:**

The Claude Code skills monetization ecosystem is real but early-stage. Key data points as of March 2026:

- Anthropic launched an official plugin marketplace in **February 2026** — the fastest-growing part of the Cowork ecosystem
- Community directories (claudemarketplaces.com, skillsmp.com, agent37.com) list 150–340+ skills
- GitHub repos like `jeremylongshore/claude-code-plugins-plus-skills` (340 plugins, 1367 skills) show open-source scale
- Paid skills typically price at **5–15 EUR** targeting specific professional workflows
- The ecosystem is still majority-free; paid segment is small but emerging

**Monetization models that work for skills:**
- **Open Core**: free skills with premium specialized variants (most applicable)
- **Hosted Access**: sell access to a running skill endpoint rather than distributing files (scales best, protects IP)
- **Professional Services**: free skills as lead gen, paid consulting/customization around them
- **Usage-Based**: token/call metering on hosted skill endpoints

**Key friction identified:** distribution requires CLI install, which kills conversion. The "Gumroad for Claude skills" problem — runtime, discoverability, and frictionless customer access — is unsolved at the platform level. Most serious monetizers are building hosted access layers on top of open skills.

**Sources:**
- [Best Claude Code Skills & Plugins (2026 Guide) | DEV Community](https://dev.to/raxxostudios/best-claude-code-skills-plugins-2026-guide-4ak4)

**Relevance to web-god:** web-god is currently open source on GitHub — it is in the right place at the right time. ## Mission 40 — After Scrollytelling: Next Paradigm

**Findings:**

Scrollytelling is not dying — it has become the baseline, which means the frontier has moved. The 2026 consensus across Webflow Blog, Figma, UX Pilot, and multiple trend reports identifies a clear evolution:

**Current state (2026):** Scroll is now "a navigation tool, not a spectacle." Sophisticated scroll-linked 3D experiences are standard for premium brands. SIGGRAPH 2026 has a dedicated Spatial Storytelling track. Atlas Obscura launched a WebXR 3D social lounge in early 2026.

**What comes next — three converging vectors:**

1. **Spatial / 3D Web Environments**: Users don't scroll through content, they walk through it. Interactive 3D product showrooms, branded environments closer to games than pages. WebXR eliminates the install barrier — it runs in-browser. The "scroll" is replaced by "movement through space."

2. **AI-Personalized Narratives**: Instead of one fixed story told to all visitors, story frameworks adapt in real time to user profile, behavior, emotional state detection, and context. Research shows 6x higher conversion and 73% higher completion rates for personalized narratives. Fully adaptive storytelling generates infinite variations of core narrative content via LLM, with conversational navigation. This is beginning to appear in brand storytelling contexts.

3. **Immersive + Conversational Hybrid**: AI-powered NPCs with conversational dialogue within WebXR environments; spatial computing that responds to real-time user interaction rather than pre-scripted triggers. SIGGRAPH 2026 is actively showcasing this territory.

**Timeline signal:** The Codrops "Spark" article (January 2026) and WebXR experiences launching now suggest the inflection point is 12–18 months out from mass adoption — early enough that positioning now is premature-but-right.

**Relevance to web-god:** The `webgod-scrollytelling` skill handles the current paradigm. The next paradigm — spatial + AI-personalized — needs new skills: a `webgod-webxr` skill for spatial storytelling, and a `webgod-narrative-ai` skill for adaptive/personalized content generation. These are 6–12 months from being actionable for most production clients, but the architecture decisions made in web-god now (agent composition, tool boundaries) should account for them.

**Action:** Create a roadmap entry for `webgod-webxr` (Three.js / A-Frame / Babylon.js + WebXR skill) and `webgod-narrative-ai` (LLM-driven adaptive content). Do not build now — validate with one real project first. Priority: **P2**, Effort: **L**

## Agent 24: Web3 Website Narrative Patterns Report

*Source: a3c42d964f6231615.output*

I'll search for web3 website narrative patterns across multiple angles to understand how blockchain projects communicate differently from traditional SaaS.
## Web3 Website Narrative Patterns Report

**Key Findings: How Web3 Projects Communicate Differently**

Web3 projects fundamentally diverge from traditional SaaS in four ways:

**1. Hero Positioning Shift**
Unlike SaaS (product as hero), web3 positions the *audience* as the protagonist, with technology serving as a guide to transformation. Copy leads with "what's possible" rather than "how it works."

**2. Trust Paradox**
While blockchain promises trustlessness, web3 messaging actually *builds* trust through centralized anchors—recognized exchanges, founder credibility, audited contracts. This contradicts decentralization rhetoric but reflects user psychology.

**3. Layered Accessibility**
Web3 sites employ multi-tier messaging for varying crypto literacy (crypto literacy rose from 11% to 31.8% awareness 2022-2024). Technical audiences see blockchain fundamentals; newcomers see community and transformation narrative.

**4. Community-as-Product**
Crypto copy emphasizes peer-to-peer neoliberalism and technical sovereignty—framing users as agents in a shared ideological movement, not consumers. Language privileges "believers," "communities," and "movement" over customer segments.

**Distinct Narrative Elements:**
- Transparency over hype (responding to VC crash skepticism)
- Regulatory acknowledgment (positioning seriousness vs. noise)
- Decentralization claims with centralized verification (team/audit trust)
- Economic and legal literacy layering

**SaaS vs Web3 Comparison:**
SaaS emphasizes efficiency, ROI, feature comparison. Web3 emphasizes ideology, governance participation, and financial sovereignty—appealing to libertarian and anti-institutional sentiment alongside genuine tech innovation.

## Agent 25: Web3/DeFi Dashboard UX Writing Challenges

*Source: a3f2b0cc59d72a42c.output*

I'll search for web3/DeFi dashboard UX writing challenges and copy patterns.
## Web3/DeFi Dashboard UX Writing Challenges

**Terminology Translation**
The biggest copy challenge: blockchain jargon alienates users. Terms like "gas fees," "seed phrases," "smart contracts," and "approvals" have no Web2 equivalents. Best practice: replace "mnemonic phrase" with "secret phrase," explain gas fees only at point-of-action using progressive disclosure, and describe approvals plainly as "Allow this app to use your tokens."

**Gas Fee Accessibility**
Gas fees represent Web3's steepest UX cliff—they have no Web2 parallel and confuse most users. One solution: wallet abstraction with paymasters enables apps to subsidize gas, removing this barrier entirely. For transparent pricing, use contextual help and real-time cost estimates rather than long tutorials.

**Transaction Status Communication**
Blockchain's asynchronous nature (transactions taking minutes to hours) demands clear visual feedback. Users need transparent status stages and honest wait-time expectations. Zerion exemplifies this with real-time transaction tracking. Progress indicators and receipt confirmation (success/failure states) reduce anxiety.

**Token Approval Risk Warnings**
Approvals are a critical UX failure: users often don't understand they're granting indefinite contract access. MetaMask now clarifies setApprovalForAll consequences; Web3 Antivirus color-codes risk levels (green/yellow/red). Best practice: always show explicit permission scope and enable easy revocation.

**Building Trust Through Copy**
Calm reassurance matters. Users feel vulnerable signing blockchain transactions. Effective copy acknowledges emotion, provides reassuring warnings, and uses plain language consistently. Following WCAG accessibility guidelines ensures blockchain UX isn't exclusive.

**Sources**
- [10 Design Challenges in Web3](https://arounda.agency/blog/10-design-challenges-in-web3)
- [UX Writing for Web3 Onboarding](https://medium.com/@onyinyemodebe/over-the-past-year-we-witnessed-a-remarkable-surge-in-the-adoption-of-decentralized-technology-008e06526389)
- [DeFi Wallet UX Design](https://vocal.media/education/how-to-design-a-wallet-ux-for-de-fi-managing-transactions-approvals-and-risks)
- [Web3 Transaction Lifecycle & Status](https://medium.com/tanooki-labs/web3-ux-transaction-statuses-b828afe8d7af)
- [Making Gas Fees Accessible](https://www.netswagger.com/blog/web3-ux-design)
- [Token Approvals Security](https://beincrypto.com/hidden-danger-wallet-token-approvals-explained/)

## Agent 26: Research Summary: AI Agent System Architecture Best Practices

*Source: a3fbbf61d03625816.output*

I'll search for current best practices in AI agent system design for you.
## Research Summary: AI Agent System Architecture Best Practices

**Findings on Web-God's 15-Agent Architecture:**

### 1. **Agent Count: 15 May Be Over-Engineered**
Industry consensus from [Agilesoftlabs](https://www.agilesoftlabs.com/blog/2026/03/multi-agent-ai-systems-enterprise-guide) and [Vellum](https://vellum.ai/blog/multi-agent-systems-building-with-context-engineering) recommends **starting with 1 primary agent + 2 subagents, scaling up only as needed**. The [Coding Agent Teams report](https://devops.com/coding-agent-teams-the-next-frontier-in-ai-assisted-software-development/) suggests successful configurations use 5-6 agents (frontend, backend, testing, review, team lead). 15 specialized agents likely creates **coordination overhead that exceeds benefit**.

### 2. **Specialization is Correct, But Granularity Matters**
[Microsoft Azure's framework](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/architecture/ai-ml/guide/ai-agent-design-patterns) confirms specialization outperforms generalization. However, [DevOps.com](https://devops.com/coding-agent-teams-the-next-frontier-in-ai-assisted-software-development/) shows that effective systems organize by *workflow stage* (write → test → review) rather than *domain*, suggesting web-god's 15 domain silos may fragment work unnecessarily.

### 3. **Conductor → Specialist → Validator is Standard**
[Addy Osmani's architecture guide](https://addyosmani.com/blog/code-agent-orchestra/) and [Azure's patterns](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/architecture/ai-ml/guide/ai-agent-design-patterns) confirm this exact pattern is industry-standard. Web-god appears aligned here.

### 4. **Hybrid Knowledge Model Wins**
[Anthropic's 2026 report](https://resources.anthropic.com/hubfs/2026%20Agentic%20Coding%20Trends%20Report.pdf?hsLang=en) and [Stack Overflow research](https://stackoverflow.blog/2026/03/16/domain-expertise-still-wanted-the-latest-trends-in-ai/) show successful systems combine **hard-coded domain expertise with dynamic tool selection and RAG**—not pure dynamic search.

### 5. **CrewAI/LangGraph Patterns**
[DataCamp's framework comparison](https://www.datacamp.com/tutorial/crewai-vs-langgraph-vs-autogen) shows both frameworks recommend **combining a supervisor graph (LangGraph) with role-based workers (CrewAI)**, not isolated agents. Web-god's structure aligns with this.

**Verdict:** The conductor-specialist-validator pattern is sound, but 15 agents likely over-fragments responsibility. Consolidating to 6-8 agents (grouped by workflow, not pure domain) would reduce coordination costs while maintaining specialization benefits.

## Agent 27: CSP Evolution Report - March 2026

*Source: a48521c3b56bce511.output*

I'll search for the latest CSP evolution information for you.
## CSP Evolution Report - March 2026

**CSP Level 3 Status:**
CSP Level 3 remains a W3C Working Draft with partial browser support (Chrome 59+, Firefox 58+, Safari 15.4+, Edge 79+). Key additions: undeprecated frame-src, new worker-src directive, rewritten per Fetch spec. [W3C CSP3](https://www.w3.org/TR/CSP3/) | [MDN Guide](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/Guides/CSP)

**Trusted Types Adoption:**
Implemented in Chrome/Edge since 2020, but Safari support remains absent. W3C polyfill available for broader compatibility. Production-ready via `require-trusted-types-for 'script'` directive. [MDN Trusted Types API](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/Trusted_Types_API) | [Directive Ref](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/Reference/Headers/Content-Security-Policy/trusted-types)

**2026 Best Practices:**
1. **Nonce/hash-based approach** for script-src (strict CSP preferred)
2. **Trusted Types** for injection sink protection
3. **Frame-ancestors** replaces deprecated X-Frame-Options
4. **Report-to directive** for violation reporting (use Reporting-Endpoints header)
5. **Set CSP on all responses**, not just document

**Template Updates Needed:**
- Add worker-src if using Service Workers
- Implement Trusted Types if handling user-generated content
- Migrate X-Frame-Options to frame-ancestors
- Use report-to for centralized CSP violation monitoring

[OWASP CSP Cheat Sheet](https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Content_Security_Policy_Cheat_Sheet.html) | [CSP Quick Reference](https://content-security-policy.com/)

## Research Findings: AI Agent Differentiation in Web-God

### 1. AI Security Audit Agents - ESTABLISHED & CROWDED
Multiple players exist in automated STRIDE threat modeling: [STRIDE GPT](https://stridegpt.streamlit.app/), [Arrows (SANS hackathon project)](https://fuzzinglabs.com/ai-threat-modeling-arrows/), and [STRIDER](https://github.com/AI-Security-Research-Group/strider). This **narrows commodity status**: classical STRIDE is common; AI-agent-aware STRIDE is novel. GitHub Copilot also added [native security scanning](https://github.blog/changelog/2025-10-28-copilot-coding-agent-now-automatically-validates-code-security-and-quality/), but it's surface-level code validation, not threat modeling.

Web-god's SEO agent offers no differentiation here—market is mature with established competitors offering comparable audit depth.

### 3. AI Testing Agents - MATURING BUT FRAGMENTED
[Testim, Mabl, and QA Wolf](https://www.qawolf.com/blog/the-12-best-ai-testing-tools-in-2026) handle test generation and self-healing execution. Web-god's Testing Diamond framing is **novel positioning** but [Pyramid dominance persists in 2025](https://qalified.com/blog/test-pyramid-for-engineering-teams/).

Snyk integrates [AI security fixing alongside Copilot](https://docs.snyk.io/integrations/snyk-studio-agentic-integrations/quickstart-guides-for-snyk-studio/github-copilot-guide), proving specialized agents add ROI. However, general-purpose LLMs increasingly handle these tasks—differentiation requires domain expertise (threat modeling, SEO audits, test strategy).

### Verdict
**Security (ASTRIDE)**: Differentiated. **SEO**: Commodity. **Testing (Diamond)**: Novel framing, limited industry adoption.

## W3C Design Tokens Specification Status - March 2026

**Status: STABLE & PRODUCTION-READY**

The W3C Design Tokens Community Group released the first stable version (2025.10) on October 28, 2025. It is NOT a W3C Standard but a Community Group Report with broad vendor adoption.

**Standard Format:**
JSON-based format supporting theming, multi-brand support, modern color spaces (Display P3, Oklch, CSS Color Module 4), and rich token relationships (aliases, inheritance). Style Dictionary v4 now accepts DTCG spec as source format alongside its legacy format.

**Tool Ecosystem:**
10+ tools actively support/implement: Figma, Penpot, Sketch, Framer, Knapsack, Supernova, zeroheight, Style Dictionary, Tokens Studio, and Terrazzo. Figma's 2026 updates include native Git integration and AI-generated tokens syncing to production.

**Recommendation for web-god:**
ADOPT. The design-system-architect should target DTCG 2025.10 format as primary export target. It's battle-tested, vendor-neutral, and future-proof with broad ecosystem support. Use Style Dictionary v4+ for multi-platform compilation.

## Agent 30: Scrollytelling Narrative Techniques Report

*Source: a4e2e89437dec78e2.output*

I'll search for scrollytelling-specific narrative techniques across multiple sources.
## Scrollytelling Narrative Techniques Report

**Narrative Techniques for Scroll:**
- **Narrative beats** as atomic storytelling units—restructure content into scroll-triggered moments that maintain coherence while controlling pacing and format
- **Progressive disclosure**: reveal information gradually through scroll position, maintaining reader curiosity and preventing cognitive overload
- **Emotional progression**: build investment across the scroll journey with sensory language complementing visuals and interactive triggers

**Scroll vs. Static Pages:**
Scrollytelling transforms passive reading into active participation. Traditional pages present complete information; scrollytelling synchronizes narrative events with scroll position, using parallax, fade-ins, and animations as narrative devices rather than decorations. Pacing becomes reader-controlled—scroll speed defines beat duration.

**Scroll Pacing Affects Story Beats:**
- Shorter paragraphs and transitional phrases guide readers between sections
- Whitespace strategically pauses readers to reflect on story beats
- Animation timing syncs with narrative events (like combat in games aligning with plot momentum)
- Social media conversion research shows text shortening within beats creates faster, more engaging pacing than longer static copy

**Timing & Progressive Disclosure:**
CSS scroll() and view() timelines progress based on element visibility inside a scroller. Each scroll-triggered effect must serve narrative purpose—gratuitous animation distracts. Reveals work through fade-ins, parallax rate variations, and staggered content materialization.

**Critical Difference:** Scrollytelling requires cinematographic thinking, not just editorial. Content hierarchy changes: scroll position becomes the primary narrative input, transforming the reader from passive observer to active navigator controlling story momentum.

## Agent 31: Database Trends 2026 - Research Report

*Source: a513758fd769d8bf3.output*

I'll search for current database trends for web applications in 2026.
## Database Trends 2026 - Research Report

**Key Winners:**

**Serverless Postgres Dominates.** Neon leads with instant branching, scale-to-zero compute, and 15-25% price cuts post-Databricks acquisition (May 2025). Supabase wins for full-stack platforms combining auth, storage, and realtime. PlanetScale shifted premium (removed free tier) but now offers both MySQL and Postgres.

**Edge SQLite Emerging.** Turso/libSQL enables distributed SQLite at the edge—databases everywhere (servers, browsers, devices). Lighter alternative to Postgres for latency-sensitive apps. Embedded replicas sync with central instances.

**Competitive Landscape:**
- Neon: Best standalone serverless Postgres (scale-to-zero, branching)
- Supabase: Best integrated BaaS (auth + storage bundled)
- PlanetScale: Enterprise MySQL/Postgres with branching
- Turso: Edge-optimized SQLite replication
- AWS Aurora: New express config for instant serverless setup

**Recommendation for Backend Agent:**
Default to **Neon for standard APIs** (serverless, instant dev environments). Use **Supabase for full-stack SaaS** (built-in auth/storage). Consider **Turso for edge-native apps** with distributed data. Avoid PlanetScale unless scaling to YouTube-scale or need premium support.

- [Neon Serverless Guide](https://encore.dev/articles/neon-serverless-postgres)
- [Turso & libSQL Overview](https://turso.tech/)

## Agent 32: Portfolio & Personal Brand Narrative Report

## Portfolio & Personal Brand Narrative Report

**Narrative Frameworks:**
Portfolio websites function as curated stories that reveal skills, process, and personality. The **StoryBrand Framework** positions the customer (not your brand) as the hero, with you as their guide—a seven-part messaging model effective for about pages and personal branding. Case studies are the core storytelling vehicle: lead with impact ("increased engagement by 30%") rather than chronology to demonstrate decision-making and process.

**About Page Elements:**
Effective about pages use first-person voice with conversational tone, covering: who you are, what you do, why you do it, and what motivates you. Include personal touches—visuals, music playlists, unique contact forms—to create deeper emotional connection. Conciseness matters; focus clarity over length.

**Personal Value Proposition:**
Your value proposition answers three questions: What You Do (expertise/capabilities), How You Do It (unique methodology), Why It Matters (tangible benefits). Avoid generic language; instead highlight unique selling points, express opinions, and showcase relevant, current work. Authenticity requires avoiding copied claims and outdated projects.

**Visual Storytelling:**
Every design element (fonts, colors, spacing) communicates. Use composition hierarchy to guide readers; alternate between wide shots (full layouts, context) and close-ups (details, typography). Process sketches, mood boards, and before-and-after comparisons illustrate the concept-to-completion journey.

**Key Resources:**
- [Crafting a Narrative: Mastering Storytelling in Your Design Portfolio](https://dribbble.com/stories/2024/03/18/crafting-a-narrative-mastering-storytelling-in-your-design-portfolio)
- [StoryBrand Framework Guide](https://localgrowth.com/the-ultimate-guide-to-the-storybrand-framework-and-how-to-use-it-on-your-website/)
- [Personal Value Propositions Overview](https://www.interaction-design.org/literature/topics/personal-value-propositions)
- [How to Write a Perfect About Me Page](https://www.thebalancemoney.com/how-to-write-about-me-page-examples-4142367)

## Mission 9 — CSS Scroll-Driven Animations

**Findings:**

- **Chrome/Edge 115+**: Full support since mid-2023. `animation-timeline: scroll()` and `view()`, `animation-range`, `scroll-timeline`, `view-timeline` all stable.
- **Safari**: Landed in Safari 18 (late 2024) and Safari 26 (2026 beta). Now effectively widely available on WebKit.
- **Firefox**: Still behind a flag as of March 2026. NOT enabled by default. However, scroll-driven animations are a **formal Interop 2026 focus area**, meaning Firefox has committed to shipping it without a flag — expected within 2026. Once it ships in Firefox it will reach Baseline status.
- **Polyfill**: The official [flackr/scroll-timeline polyfill](https://github.com/flackr/scroll-timeline) covers Firefox and older Safari. Used in production today (e.g., hartregie.nl).
- **New properties since Chrome 115**: `animation-range-start` / `animation-range-end` for fine control; `view-timeline-inset` for adjusting entry/exit offsets; `timeline-scope` for cross-element timeline sharing.
- **Performance**: Runs on the compositor thread for `transform`/`opacity` — no main-thread blocking, 60fps even under heavy JS.
- **Production readiness**: Yes, with `@supports (animation-timeline: view())` for progressive enhancement + polyfill for Firefox. Use `@supports` guard + polyfill = full cross-browser coverage today.

**Sources:**
- [MDN CSS Scroll-Driven Animations](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/Guides/Scroll-driven_animations)
- [Smashing Magazine Introduction](https://www.smashingmagazine.com/2024/12/introduction-css-scroll-driven-animations/)
- [Interop 2026 — CSS-Tricks](https://css-tricks.com/interop-2026/)
- [Launching Interop 2026 — Mozilla Hacks](https://hacks.mozilla.org/2026/02/launching-interop-2026/)
- [flackr/scroll-timeline polyfill](https://github.com/flackr/scroll-timeline)
- [DevToolbox Complete Guide](https://devtoolbox.dedyn.io/blog/css-scroll-animations-guide)
- [Mozilla Connect — Firefox flag status](https://connect.mozilla.org/t5/discussions/why-doesn-t-firefox-support-the-css-animation-timeline/m-p/63761)

**Relevance to web-god:** Directly impacts the `webgod-scrollytelling` skill and any `frontend-architect` agent guidance on animation. The spec is mature; only Firefox is the holdout, and that is actively being resolved via Interop 2026.

**Action:** Update `webgod-scrollytelling` and CSS animation guidance to recommend `@supports` progressive enhancement + the flackr polyfill. Mark as production-ready with caveats. Include `animation-range`, `view-timeline-inset`, and `timeline-scope` in the reference docs. Priority: **P1**, Effort: **S**

## Mission 10 — View Transitions API

**Findings:**

- **Single-document (SPA)**: Baseline across Chrome 111+, Edge 111+, Safari 18+, Firefox 146+ (partial). Global coverage ~78% as of March 2026.
- **Cross-document (MPA)**: Chrome 126+, Edge 126+, Safari 18.5+, Firefox 146+ (partial). Opt-in via `@view-transition { navigation: auto; }` in CSS — both origin-same documents must opt in.
- **Next.js native support**: Next.js 16 ships an **experimental** `viewTransition: true` flag in `next.config.js`. As of March 31, 2026 it is still marked experimental/not production-recommended.
- **React 19.2 integration**: Released March 2026 alongside Next.js 16, shipping a native `startViewTransition` hook — eliminates need for third-party libs for page transitions.
- **App Router behavior**: Route transitions automatically trigger view transitions when the flag is enabled; no manual `startTransition` wrapping needed.
- **Community libraries**: [`next-view-transitions`](https://github.com/shuding/next-view-transitions) by Shu Ding remains available for simpler use cases.
- **Cross-document readiness**: Working in Chrome/Edge/Safari today. Firefox partial support since Firefox 146. Can be treated as progressive enhancement for MPA setups.

**Sources:**
- [MDN View Transition API](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/View_Transition_API)

**Relevance to web-god:** Should be included in `webgod-frontend` skill guidance and `frontend-architect` agent. Enables native page transitions without GSAP or Framer Motion for many cases — significant DX and performance win. The experimental Next.js flag means guidance should note production caveats but encourage adoption for Chrome/Safari-primary audiences.

## Mission 11 — React Server Components + Partial Prerendering

**Findings:**

- **PPR stability**: PPR is now **stable** in Next.js 16. The experimental `experimental.ppr` flag is gone. It is now implemented through the **Cache Components** model (`"use cache"` directive). Enabled via `cacheComponents` option in `next.config.ts`.
- **Cache Components model**: Replaces the old implicit caching system with explicit per-component/function cache declarations using `"use cache"`. This is the new default mental model for Next.js 16+ apps.
- **Key 2026 RSC patterns**:
  1. **Static shell + dynamic islands**: Pre-render layout/nav at build time; wrap dynamic content in `<Suspense>` with skeleton fallbacks. Static shell served from CDN edge; dynamic content streams in.
  2. **Leaf-level "use client"**: Push client directives to the lowest-level interactive leaf components; keep layouts, containers, and data-fetching components as Server Components.
  3. **Parallel data-fetching**: Split async data dependencies into sibling Server Components so they resolve in parallel, not sequentially.
  4. **Streaming architecture**: React's streaming protocol streams HTML chunks as each dynamic Suspense boundary resolves — browser paints static shell while server resolves dynamic parts.
- **Sitepoint 2026 guide**: Confirms streaming + RSC composition as the dominant production pattern.

**Sources:**
- [Next.js 16 blog post](https://nextjs.org/blog/next-16)
- [Next.js PPR Getting Started](https://nextjs.org/docs/15/app/getting-started/partial-prerendering)
- [Vercel PPR blog](https://vercel.com/blog/partial-prerendering-with-next-js-creating-a-new-default-rendering-model)
- [Sitepoint RSC Streaming 2026](https://www.sitepoint.com/react-server-components-streaming-performance-2026/)
- [Jishu Labs Next.js 15 & 16 migration guide](https://jishulabs.com/blog/nextjs-15-16-features-migration-guide-2026)
- [DEV Community PPR deep dive](https://dev.to/pockit_tools/nextjs-partial-prerendering-ppr-deep-dive-how-it-works-when-to-use-it-and-why-it-changes-48dk)

**Relevance to web-god:** The `frontend-architect` agent and `webgod-frontend` skill's rendering guidance needs updating. PPR is no longer experimental — it is the recommended default rendering strategy. The `"use cache"` directive pattern is the new idiom to teach.

**Action:** Update `frontend-architect` agent and `webgod-frontend` skill to reflect: PPR stable via `"use cache"`, Cache Components as the new model, parallel sibling Server Components pattern, leaf-level `"use client"`. Remove any references to `experimental.ppr`. Priority: **P0**, Effort: **M**

## Agent 34: Cognitive Biases in Web Narrative: Ethical Leverage & Dark Pattern Warnings

*Source: a59e6dc7e506cb98c.output*

I'll conduct web research on cognitive biases in web design and narrative, focusing on ethical leverage and dark pattern warnings.
## Cognitive Biases in Web Narrative: Ethical Leverage & Dark Pattern Warnings

**Ethically Leverageable Biases:**

1. **Anchoring Bias** - Display higher-priced alternatives first to make lower options seem valuable. Example: Williams-Sonoma's $275 bread maker sold better after introducing a $429 model. Use authentically: show real price comparisons, not inflated anchors.

2. **Loss Aversion** - Frame messaging around what users *lose* if they don't act (up to 32% conversion increase). Genuine scarcity ("5 left in stock") outperforms fake urgency. Ethical boundaries: base on real constraints.

3. **Framing Effect** - Loss-framed copy outperforms gain-framed. A study found 93% of students registered to avoid a late fee versus 67% for early-bird discounts. Landing page example: "Is your yard lowering property value?" generated 24% higher CTR than benefit-focused framing.

4. **Social Proof & Authority** - Leverage genuine testimonials and expert endorsement. Effectiveness multiplies when authentic; credibility evaporates if discovered as fake.

5. **Default Effect** - Users prefer pre-selected options. Apply ethically by making beneficial defaults (e.g., privacy-protective settings), not predatory ones.

6. **Peak-End Rule** - Optimize final touchpoints. Users remember peak moments and endings most vividly.

**Dark Pattern Warnings:**

The line between persuasion and manipulation lies in *intent and authenticity*. Dark patterns exploit biases through:
- Fake scarcity/urgency
- Obstructed unsubscribe paths
- Manufactured social proof
- Sunk cost manipulation

GDPR, CCPA, and regulatory bodies now target deceptive design. Users detect manipulation; brands suffer lasting damage.

**Key Sources:**
- [RIVA: Ethical UX Design & Cognitive Biases](https://rivasolutionsinc.com/insights/ethical-ux-design-cognitive-biases/)
- [Growth.Design: 106 Cognitive Biases](https://growth.design/psychology)
- [Invesp: Price Anchoring](https://www.invespcro.com/blog/13-loss-aversion-marketing-strategies-to-increase-conversions/)
- [The Decision Lab: Anchoring Bias](https://thedecisionlab.com/biases/anchoring-bias)
- [Formal Psychology: Dark Patterns](https://formalpsychology.com/dark-patterns-web-design-psychology/)
- [Lead Alchemists: Framing Effect in Marketing](https://www.leadalchemists.com/marketing-psychology/framing-effect/)
