The PDF is fully extracted across all 20 pages. Here is the complete research report.

---

# The S.T.A.R. UX Framework — Research Report

## 1. Peak-End Rule Application

Kahneman's Peak-End Rule states that humans judge an experience by two points only: the **Peak** (most intense emotional moment, positive or negative) and the **End** (how it concluded) — not the average of all moments.

Digital application operates on three levers:

- **Engineer Positive Peaks** — Success States with celebratory motion anchor accomplishment as the memory trace.
- **Mitigate Negative Peaks** — Gamified 404s and engaging Loading Sequences exploit the **Service Recovery Paradox**: a failure resolved delightfully produces more loyalty than no failure at all.
- **Curate the End** — "Year in Review" / Wrapped-style sessions are high-fidelity shareable events that close the narrative loop.

The strategic implication: most "peaks" in a digital lifecycle are currently *unplanned and negative* (404s, wait states, failed payments). STAR engineering deliberately plants positive peaks at known high-stakes moments.

---

## 2. The 5 STAR Mechanisms — Digital Translations

| Analog (Duarte) | Digital Translation |
|---|---|
| Memorable Dramatization | Interactive Simulation — user "plays" content rather than reads |
| Repeatable Sound Bites | Micro-copy + sonic branding (synced audio via Web Audio API) |
| Evocative Visuals | Cinematic Motion Design — WebGL depth, particle systems, HDRI lighting |
| Emotive Storytelling | Data Scrollytelling — narrative pacing replaces static tables |
| Shocking Statistics | Insight Reveal — progressive disclosure of data (trend first, number second) |

---

## 3. The 20 STAR Moment Types — Full Taxonomy

### Category I: Onboarding Celebrations (Concepts 1–4)
| # | Name | Emotional Trigger |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | "Hero's Equipment" (Contextual Avatar Assembly) | Identity Construction & Agency |
| 2 | "Interactive Signature" (The Pact) | Commitment & Ritual |
| 3 | "Collaborative High-Five" (Sync Detection) | Belonging & Social Proof |
| 4 | "Holographic Unboxing" (AR Integration) | Surprise & Tangibility |

### Category II: Success States (Concepts 5–8)
| # | Name | Emotional Trigger |
|---|---|---|
| 5 | "Growth Garden" (Procedural Achievement) | Nurturing & Accumulation |
| 6 | "Sonic Brand Symphony" (Synesthetic Reward) | Harmony & Resolution |
| 7 | "Velocity Tunnel" (Momentum Visualizer) | Flow State & Speed |
| 8 | "Global Ripple" (Impact Map) | Connection & Consequence |

### Category III: Gamified 404 Pages (Concepts 9–12)
| # | Name | Emotional Trigger |
|---|---|---|
| 9 | "Lost Dimension" (Playable Micro-Game) | Playfulness & Stress Relief |
| 10 | "Glitch Art" (Interactive Distortion) | Curiosity & Restoration |
| 11 | "Time Travel" (Archive.org Tribute) | Nostalgia & Humor |
| 12 | "AI Concierge" (Conversational Recovery) | Empathy & Companionship |

### Category IV: Loading Sequences (Concepts 13–16)
| # | Name | Emotional Trigger |
|---|---|---|
| 13 | "Generative Construction Crew" (Narrative Progress) | Storytelling & Scale |
| 14 | "Data Stream Decryption" (The Matrix Effect) | Sophistication & Power |
| 15 | "Physics Sandbox" (Waiting Room Toy) | Joy & Distraction |
| 16 | "Travel Montage" (Contextual Journey) | Anticipation & Context |

### Category V: Data Visualization Reveals (Concepts 17–20)
| # | Name | Emotional Trigger |
|---|---|---|
| 17 | "Personal Constellation" (Node Connection) | Pattern Recognition & Beauty |
| 18 | "Sediment Layers" (Geological History) | Legacy & Permanence |
| 19 | "City Builder" (Metaphorical Stats) | Constructiveness |
| 20 | "Narrative Thread" (Unspooling) | Continuity & Story |

---

## 4. Tech Stack Decision Framework

| Tool | Best For | Interactivity | Performance | File Size |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Rive** | Complex apps, state-driven interactions, character animation | High | High efficiency | Ultra low |
| **Lottie** | Linear playback, landing pages, simple UI loops, dynamic text injection | Low/Medium | Moderate | High (JSON) |
| **Three.js / R3F** | Immersive 3D environments, physics simulations, data-driven 3D | High (custom) | Dev-dependent | High (models) |
| **Spline** | Rapid no-code 3D elements, designer-led interactive embeds | Medium | Moderate | Moderate |

**Decision rule:** Rive is the default for all 2D interactive STAR moments (10–15x smaller than Lottie, built-in state machines, skeletal animation/Bones). Lottie is retained for linear playback and dynamic text injection at runtime (e.g., Concept 16 "Travel Montage" injecting city names). Three.js/R3F is reserved for immersive 3D environments where application state must drive geometry directly (e.g., user data driving 3D bar chart height). Spline bridges the designer-developer gap for 3D vignettes without shader code.

---

## 5. Accessibility Requirements

The document is explicit: **accessibility is non-negotiable.**

- All STAR implementations must hook into `prefers-reduced-motion` media query.
- When reduced motion is requested, the STAR moment **must fallback** to a static, high-quality illustration or a simplified fade — preserving "delight" without inducing vestibular disorders.
- Heavy visualizations must offload logic to **Web Workers** via Offscreen Canvas to keep the main thread free for UI responsiveness.
- Performance budget is strict: any loading sequence that drops the frame rate below **60fps defeats its own purpose**.
- Concept 15 (Physics Sandbox): particle count capped at 200 for mobile performance.

---

## 6. Implementation Patterns

**State Machine Pattern (Rive):** Designer defines state machine inside the .riv file. Developer sends named input triggers; animation handles all transitions internally. Used in Concepts 3, 12, 13.

**Shader Uniform Binding (Three.js):** Application metric (e.g., APM for Concept 7 "Velocity Tunnel") is bound directly to a GLSL `uniform float uSpeed`. The render loop reads live data and passes it to the GPU each frame.

**L-System Proceduralism (Concept 5):** Task ID seeds the random number generator for L-System branching strings, ensuring determinism — the same task always produces the same unique plant. GSAP DrawSVG animates stroke growth with `elastic.out` easing.

**Data-Attribute Theme Switching (Concept 11):** A single DOM structure swaps a `data-era` attribute on `<body>`. All CSS cascades from attribute selectors — zero JS rendering cost.

**Audio-Driven Visuals (Concept 6):** Web Audio API `AnalyserNode` provides FFT data each frame. Bass frequencies drive visual scale; treble drives brightness. Audio leads, visuals follow — prevents sync drift that afflicts pre-baked video approaches.

**Progressive Disclosure / Scrollytelling:** Scroll position drives simulation `alpha` (Concept 17) or SVG `stroke-dashoffset` (Concept 20) via GSAP ScrollTrigger. Trend is revealed before the number is shown.

**Implementation Roadmap (from Chapter 8):**
1. Audit the Peaks — map emotional valleys and uncelebrated peaks in the current user journey.
2. Prototype with Purpose — use Spline or Rive Editor before touching code; STAR moments are defined by timing and physics, not pixels.
3. Governance & Metrics — measure Retention (onboarding return rate) and Sentiment (NPS delta post-success state).

---

**Source:** "The S.T.A.R. UX Framework: Engineering Memorable Digital Experiences" — 20-page catalog, 8 chapters, 29 citations. All 20 concepts fully cataloged above.

## Agent 64: Eugene Schwartz's 5 Stages of Awareness

*Source: a9999bc47d372898b.output*

I'll search for Eugene Schwartz's 5 stages of awareness for web copy.
## Eugene Schwartz's 5 Stages of Awareness

**The Framework**: Eugene Schwartz's 1966 *Breakthrough Advertising* introduced the 5-level customer awareness model. Before writing any copy, identify your audience's awareness stage—it determines your entire message strategy.

### The 5 Levels & Copy Strategy

1. **Unaware**: No problem recognition. Copy: evocative images, avoid jargon, suggest possibilities without overselling features.
2. **Problem Aware**: Recognize problem, seek solutions. Copy: empathetic language, create intrigue around the solution.
3. **Solution Aware**: Know solutions exist, comparing options. Copy: testimonials, case studies, proof of superiority.
4. **Product Aware**: Know your product, hesitant. Copy: discounts, offers, urgency, comparative advantages.
5. **Most Aware**: Ready to buy, need final push. Copy: precise pricing, irresistible offer, clear purchase path.

### Diagnosing Your Audience's Level

Ask these questions: Do they recognize the problem exists? Do they know solutions are available? Are they familiar with competing products? Have they heard of *your* product? The answer progression reveals their awareness stage and dictates landing page structure—headlines, proof points, and CTAs all shift accordingly.

**Why This Matters**: Misaligned messaging (e.g., detailed feature lists for the unaware) kills conversions. Schwartz's model ensures every element of your landing page resonates with where prospects actually are.

---

### Key Sources
- [Breakthrough Marketing Secrets](https://www.breakthroughmarketingsecrets.com/blog/what-eugene-schwartzs-market-awareness-model-missed-completely/)
- [Between the Lines Copy](https://betweenthelinescopy.com/blog/stages-of-awareness/)
- [Lead Generation Economy](https://www.leadgen-economy.com/blog/five-stages-awareness-lead-generation/)
- [Outbrain](https://www.outbrain.com/blog/the-5-stages-of-customer-awareness-and-how-to-create-content-for-each/)
- [Game of Conversions](https://gameofconversions.com/customer-awareness-stages/)
- [B-PlanNow](https://b-plannow.com/en/the-schwartz-pyramid-guide-to-the-5-levels-of-customer-awareness/)

## Scroll Engagement UX Research Report (2026)

### Latest Key Data
- **Scrollytelling Impact**: Interactive scroll narratives increase engagement by 85%, boost e-commerce conversions by 8.4%, and drive direct product conversions up to 40%
- **Video Completion Rates**: 50%+ completion on short-form video is critical; Connected TV achieves 94-98% completion on non-skippable inventory
- **Platform Benchmarks**: TikTok targets 75%+ full video completion; YouTube Shorts introduced view counting tied to scroll interaction

### What Kills Engagement
- Infinite scrolling on goal-directed tasks (e-commerce search) breaks user experience; works only for homogeneous content streams
- Janky scrolling and high latency worse than animations; accessibility (prefers-reduced-motion) essential for compliance
- Burying insights in walls of text; progressive revelation with scroll-triggered reveals outperforms static layouts

- **Scroll Depth + Attention Time**: Google Analytics 4, Hotjar measure how far users scroll and dwell time
- **Zero-UI Interactions**: Gesture/scroll-driven navigation replacing traditional buttons
- **Scroll as Narrative**: Story progression tied directly to scrolling creates emotional investment and participant engagement

## Research Report: Scrollytelling Frameworks & Your Web-God Approach

**Leading Frameworks (2025-2026):**
GSAP ScrollTrigger dominates as the industry standard (now 100% free), with [Lenis](https://lenis.darkroom.engineering/) emerging as the lightweight smooth-scroll default (2.13kb, framework-agnostic). [Motion.dev](https://motion.dev) leads React/Next.js, and [Anime.js v4](https://animejs.org/) offers modular physics. These are production tools at major publishers (NYT, National Geographic, The Pudding).

**AI Tools:**
[Scrollytelling.ai](https://scrollytelling.ai/) claims 17x engagement boost via AI-generated narratives; [Dora](https://www.dora.run/) builds 3D sites from prompts. Most AI tooling focuses on narrative generation, not animation choreography—a gap your pipeline could fill.

**5-Agent Pipeline Assessment:**
Your Director→Choreographer→Typographer→Compositor→Auditor+Builder structure is **appropriately complex, not over-engineered.** Each agent handles distinct concerns (narrative orchestration, animation timing, typography, rendering, auditing). This mirrors professional agency workflows—[NRK's Visual Stories team](https://developer.chrome.com/blog/nrk-casestudy) uses similar departmentalization. Monolithic tools fail at specialization.

**Agency Tools:**
Top studios (Active Theory, Resn, NRK) build custom tooling, not off-the-shelf frameworks. They layer GSAP+Lenis, custom state management, and specialized teams. They're solving your exact problem.

**Duarte "Resonate":**
Not widely used in web scrollytelling—Resonate is primarily presentation methodology (structure, story arc). Scrollytelling borrowed its narrative tension (setup→build→payoff) but doesn't adopt the full framework.

**Comparison to No-Code:**
Webflow/Readymag serve marketing sites; your approach targets high-fidelity brand experiences. No-code tools lack animation choreography depth, multi-agent QA, and framework flexibility. Your system trades ease for precision.

**Conclusion:**
Your pipeline targets a real market gap—professional-grade scrollytelling with systematic quality gates, not another GSAP wrapper.

## Research Findings: AI-Powered Frontend Architecture Tools (2025-2026)

**v0 by Vercel** focuses on component generation rather than architectural guidance. It generates React/Tailwind/shadcn/ui code via chat but [doesn't tackle application architecture—components work as standalone pieces](https://skywork.ai/blog/vercel-v0-review-2025-ai-ui-code-generation-nextjs/), leaving state management and system design to developers. However, Vercel has released [react-best-practices with 40+ performance rules specifically encoded for AI agents](https://www.infoq.com/news/2026/02/vercel-react-best-practices/), prioritizing waterfalls elimination, bundle size reduction, and serialization overhead.

**Cursor & Windsurf** (agentic IDEs) take a different approach. Windsurf's Cascade agent uses [graph-based reasoning to map entire codebase dependencies](https://www.qodo.ai/blog/windsurf-vs-cursor/), maintaining architectural context across files. Cursor's Background Agents run in isolated VMs. Neither explicitly encodes frontend architecture decisions—they infer from codebase patterns. Neither has a dedicated "frontend architect" agent like your web-god package.

**Bolt, Lovable, Replit Agent** generate full-stack apps but [default to happy-path implementations without explicit architecture constraints](https://emergent.sh/learn/bolt-new-vs-replit-vs-lovable-vs-emergent). They scaffold projects but require user guidance for nuanced decisions (Server Components vs Client Components, state management strategy, etc.).

**Open-source patterns** show encoding architecture in agents.md files—[structured config files written for AI agents rather than humans](https://aidevme.com/agents-md-best-practices/). [Next.js documentation now recommends Agent Skills approach](https://nextjs.org/docs/app/guides/ai-agents)—embedding compressed docs and structured workflows gives agents better context than documentation alone.

**Best practice consensus**: Encoding architecture decisions IS valuable. Generic LLMs without constraints make poor choices (Pages Router in App Router projects, wrong ORMs, suboptimal state patterns). Your approach of decision matrices and explicit agent prompts aligns with emerging industry practice. Vercel's success with react-best-practices validates this—[developers using specific performance rules see better outcomes than letting agents guess](https://medium.com/@abhinav.dobhal/agent-skills-in-next-js-the-performance-revolution-899a8fd40258).

**Key insight**: Current tools lack your "architect→builder→designer" chain. Most AI tools are generalist. Encoding Next.js App Router patterns, Server Components decision trees, and state management matrices into specialized agents fills a real gap.

## Agent 68: Accessibility in Web Narrative: Research Summary

*Source: aa390dfc4e6262a7e.output*

I'll search for information on accessibility in web narrative across multiple angles to provide a comprehensive report.
## Accessibility in Web Narrative: Research Summary

**How Accessibility Affects Narrative:**
Accessible web copy transforms narrative itself. When readability, plain language, and WCAG work together, they measurably cut cognitive load and boost task completion. Narrative becomes not just what you say, but how universally understandable you make it.

**Plain Language Requirements:**
WCAG emphasizes clear words for cognitive accessibility. Best practices include maximum five sentences per paragraph, under 25 words per sentence, and avoiding cultural metaphors that exclude non-native speakers. Plain language isn't optional—it's the foundational tool that makes WCAG standards achievable.

**Reading Level Targets:**
WCAG 3.1.5 (Level AAA) targets lower secondary education reading level. The Flesch-Kincaid test measures grade level. Simplified text benefits users with neurocognitive differences, reading disabilities, and memory impairments, broadening accessibility across audiences.

**Cognitive Load in Copy:**
Cognitive accessibility guidelines (WCAG 1.3, 3.2, 3.3) require adaptable content, predictable patterns, and input assistance. Clear language reduces mental effort; visual cues highlight important sections; consistent structure helps users focus attention.

**Inclusive Language:**
Avoid vision-centric words ("see," "watch"); use person-first language ("people with disabilities"); skip ableist terms unless quoted; accommodate multilingual audiences. Inclusive language acknowledges that diverse cognitive, linguistic, and cultural backgrounds access your content.

**Alt Text as Narrative:**
Alt text extends narrative beyond visuals. Keep it under 100 characters, context-driven (not purely descriptive). Decorative images need empty alt attributes; functional/informative images need purpose-focused text. Alt text enables screen reader users to understand the page's full story.

---

**Key Sources:**
- [WCAG in Plain English](https://www.siteimprove.com/blog/readability-plain-language-wcag/)
- [Cognitive Accessibility Guidelines](https://www.w3.org/WAI/cognitive/)
- [Inclusive Language Best Practices](https://oit.colorado.gov/accessibility/inclusive-language)
- [Alt Text Standards](https://webaim.org/techniques/alttext/)
- [Reading Level Requirements](https://www.w3.org/WAI/WCAG21/Understanding/reading-level.html)

## Mission 13 — Playwright Latest Capabilities

**Findings:**
Playwright's 2026 release cadence brings several meaningful QA improvements:

- **Playwright MCP (Model Context Protocol)**: The headline addition — an official MCP server that lets AI agents control a real browser via Playwright. This enables AI-driven test generation, debugging, and self-healing directly inside agent workflows (Claude, Copilot, Cursor, etc.).
- **AI-assisted Codegen**: Codegen now auto-generates `toBeVisible()` assertions on common UI interactions. Combined with MCP, teams can generate full E2E suites from natural-language prompts with live DOM context.
- **Component testing maturity**: Playwright supports React, Vue, Angular, and Svelte for in-browser component testing. The primary challenge in 2026 is stability in CI, not capability gaps.
- **Aria Snapshot enhancements**: New `/children` (strict matching) and `/url` (link assertions) properties improve accessibility-oriented assertions.
- **Chrome for Testing**: Playwright now defaults to Chrome for Testing builds (not Chromium), improving parity with real-user environments.
- **Trace Viewer / UI mode**: Cmd/Ctrl+F search in code editors, JSON auto-formatting in network panel, OS-synced dark/light theme.
- **Partitioned cookies**: `partitionKey` support enables accurate cookie save/restore in multi-origin test scenarios.

Component testing coverage for React/Vue/Svelte plugs directly into the frontend skill's output. Aria snapshot assertions improve accessibility test coverage with minimal effort.

---

## Mission 14 — AI-Powered Testing Tools

**Findings:**
The AI testing tool landscape in 2026 has three distinct tiers, each with different implications for web-god:

**Tier 1 — Visual AI (complement to Playwright):**
- **Applitools**: Leading visual AI platform. Uses layout-aware diffing (not pixel-by-pixel) to handle dynamic content without false positives. Integrates directly as a Playwright assertion layer.
- **Chromatic**: Component-level visual regression tied to Storybook. Enhances Playwright and Cypress with visual, accessibility, and functional checks — no new test authoring required. Nearly indispensable for design-system workflows.

**Tier 2 — Autonomous test generation / self-healing:**
- **Mabl**: Full AI agent that builds test suites from plain-English descriptions, auto-heals tests when UI changes (85% maintenance reduction claimed), and runs with unlimited parallel agents. Integrates into CI/CD automatically.
- **Blinq.io**: Autonomous test generation from requirements or user stories.

**Tier 3 — Code-generation assistants (converging on Playwright):**
- Copilot, Cursor, Claude — now standard for repo-scale test authoring via Playwright MCP. These don't replace Playwright; they extend it.

**The real competitive threat** to web-god's Playwright-centered approach is Mabl and similar no-code AI platforms that bypass Playwright entirely. However, code-first teams with design systems remain better served by Playwright + Chromatic + Applitools than by black-box SaaS tools. Self-healing via MCP is a credible open-source counterpart.

- [15 Best AI Testing Tools 2026 — VirtuosoQA](https://www.virtuosoqa.com/post/best-ai-testing-tools)
- [Applitools](https://applitools.com/)
- [Chromatic](https://www.chromatic.com/)

## Mission 15 — Design Token Interop Standards

**Findings:**
This is the most time-sensitive finding of the four missions:

- **W3C DTCG spec is now stable**: The Design Tokens Community Group published the first stable specification version `2025.10` on October 28, 2025. It is production-ready and vendor-neutral.
- **Spec features**: Full theming/multi-brand support, Display P3 and Oklch color support, rich token aliases/inheritance, cross-platform consistency.
- **Industry alignment**: Adobe, Amazon, Google, Microsoft, Meta, Figma, Framer, Shopify, Sketch, Salesforce, Sony, Disney, and 15+ others are implementing or supporting it. This is not a fringe spec — it has reached critical mass.
- **Style Dictionary v4**: Released (originally Q2 2024), now the standard toolchain. v4 ships as ESM, is browser-compatible, supports async APIs, and has **first-class DTCG format support** (`$value`, `$type`, `$description`). Tokens Studio is now a primary contributor. DTCG and legacy SD formats cannot be mixed in a single instance — teams must pick one.
- **Toolchain support**: Style Dictionary 4, Tokens Studio, Terrazzo, Penpot, Knapsack, Supernova, zeroheight all support the stable spec.

**Sources:**
- [Design Tokens Spec Reaches First Stable Version — W3C DTCG](https://www.w3.org/community/design-tokens/2025/10/28/design-tokens-specification-reaches-first-stable-version/)
- [Design Tokens Format Module 2025.10](https://www.designtokens.org/tr/drafts/format/)
- [Design Tokens Community Group](https://www.designtokens.org/)
- [Style Dictionary v4 Statement](https://styledictionary.com/versions/v4/statement/)
- [Style Dictionary DTCG Support](https://styledictionary.com/info/dtcg/)
- [Style Dictionary v4 Plan — Tokens Studio](https://tokens.studio/blog/style-dictionary-v4-plan)

**Relevance to web-god:** The `webgod-design-system` skill and `design-system-architect` agent should be updated immediately to generate tokens in DTCG format (`$value`/`$type`/`$description`) rather than any legacy format. With the spec stable and every major design tool adopting it, generating non-DTCG tokens is now a technical liability. Style Dictionary v4 is the correct toolchain target.

**Action:** Update `webgod-design-system` to output DTCG-compliant token format by default using Style Dictionary v4. Add theming/multi-brand token structure as a first-class output option. This is a correctness fix, not an enhancement. Priority: **P0**, Effort: **S**

## Mission 16 — Web Components & Framework Trends

**Findings:**
- **Web Components renaissance**: In 2026, Web Components (Custom Elements + Shadow DOM + HTML Templates) are crossing from niche to mainstream. Native browser support is complete across all evergreen browsers. Lit (Google) is the dominant lightweight authoring layer. Primary use cases: enterprise design systems (framework-agnostic component libraries) and micro-frontend architectures.
- **Framework interoperability**: React, Vue, Angular, and Svelte now have mature Web Component consumption patterns. Web Components enable true cross-framework component sharing, which is the core value proposition for design system teams.
- **Astro vs Next.js**: Cloudflare acquired Astro in January 2026, giving it enterprise backing. Astro now holds ~15% of new projects and is growing fast, winning on content sites and marketing pages (2-3x faster than Next.js in real-world benchmarks). Next.js retains ~67% enterprise share for SaaS/B2B. React Server Components narrow the performance gap but don't close it for content-first sites. One real-world case study cut 45% of JavaScript by migrating from Next.js to Astro.
- **Island architecture**: Astro's island model (most of the page is static HTML; only interactive components hydrate) is the dominant pattern for performance-sensitive content sites. Next.js App Router with RSC is the closest equivalent in the React ecosystem.
- **Non-React support**: Vue, Svelte, and vanilla JS are first-class citizens in Astro. For scrollytelling and editorial-style content, Astro + Web Components is a credible non-React path.

**Sources:**
- [Astro vs Next.js 2026 — PagePro](https://pagepro.co/blog/astro-nextjs/)
- [Next.js vs Remix vs Astro Enterprise 2026 — AgileSoftLabs](https://www.agilesoftlabs.com/blog/2026/03/nextjs-vs-remix-vs-astro-best)
- [Astro in 2026 — Cloudflare acquisition — DEV Community](https://dev.to/polliog/astro-in-2026-why-its-beating-nextjs-for-content-sites-and-what-cloudflares-acquisition-means-6kl)
- [Why We Migrated from Next.js to Astro — Medium](https://medium.com/@treonstudio/why-we-migrated-site-from-next-js-to-astro-and-cut-45-of-our-javascript-69c229c8fb95)
- [Web Components Rise — Plugintify](https://www.plugintify.com/web-components-gain-traction-browser-support-and-framework-adoption-bolster-reusability/)
- [Astro Islands Architecture — Official Docs](https://docs.astro.build/en/concepts/islands/)
- [Web Components Are the Comeback Nobody Saw Coming — The New Stack](https://thenewstack.io/web-components-are-the-comeback-nobody-saw-coming/)

**Relevance to web-god:** The `webgod-scrollytelling` skill targets a use case (content-first, performance-critical, narrative pages) where Astro now outperforms Next.js by 2-3x. Defaulting to Next.js for scrollytelling projects is no longer the correct recommendation. Web Components are the right technology for framework-agnostic design system output from `webgod-design-system`. Supporting Vue/Svelte via Astro expands the addressable audience beyond React shops.

**Action (scrollytelling):** Add Astro as a first-class target framework in `webgod-scrollytelling`, alongside or replacing Next.js for content-first projects. Priority: **P1**, Effort: **M**

**Action (design system):** Add Web Components / Lit as an optional output target in `webgod-design-system` for framework-agnostic enterprise design systems. Priority: **P2**, Effort: **M**

**Action (frontend skill):** Document Astro as the recommended framework for marketing/content sites in `webgod-frontend` skill guidance. Priority: **P2**, Effort: **S**

## Agent 70: Report: Ogilvy's Principles for Modern Web Copywriting

*Source: aac17aa3cbc104a6a.output*

I'll search for David Ogilvy's advertising principles and their application to web copy.
## Report: Ogilvy's Principles for Modern Web Copywriting

**What Survives from Print:**

Ogilvy's core principles remain remarkably durable for web copy. Headlines still dominate—five times more people read headlines than body copy, making them critical for both print and digital. The formula holds: include brand name, add a clear benefit promise, avoid wordplay, keep it 6-12 words. Long-form copy still outperforms short when properly structured with subheads to maintain interest.

The five-element hierarchy (visual → caption → headline → copy → signature) translates directly to web: imagery drives initial engagement, headlines sell the value proposition, and body copy provides substantiation.

**Modern Adaptations:**

Digital marketers have evolved Ogilvy's approach three ways:

1. **Channel Variation**: Rather than one-size-fits-all copy, web strategists now tailor messaging by platform, funnel stage, and audience segment—test and iterate at scale.

2. **Conversational Tone**: "Marketing copy is your enemy." Modern web copy sounds like conversation, not advertising, matching how target customers actually speak.

3. **Specificity Over Cleverness**: The prohibition on wordplay remains absolute; instead, digital copywriters emphasize concrete benefits, research-backed proof points, and customer testimonials.

**Still Essential:**
- Research your product and audience thoroughly before writing
- Lead with consumer benefit, not product features
- Tell a story that makes the message memorable
- Clarity wins over complexity every time

## Sources

- [11 Timeless Copywriting Tips from Ad Legend David Ogilvy](https://willfrancis.com/11-timeless-copywriting-tips-from-david-ogilvy/)
- [David Ogilvy's 7 principles of marketing](https://cultmethod.com/articles/ogilvys-principles/)
- [David Ogilvy's Principles That Apply to Web Design](https://www.puzzlehive.com/david-ogilvys-principles-that-applies-to-web-design/)
- [Online Copywriting Secrets: 18 Lessons from David Ogilvy](https://coolerinsights.com/2021/06/online-copywriting-david-ogilvy/)
- [The Science of Website Copywriting: Tips from David Ogilvy](https://qualaroo.com/blog/the-science-of-website-copywriting-tips-from-david-ogilvy/)

## Agent 71: Report: When Narrative Hurts UX

*Source: ab0773c6be54fcaa2.output*

I'll search for insights on when narrative and storytelling hurt UX, focusing on functional design principles.
## Report: When Narrative Hurts UX

**The Core Problem:** Narrative-driven design fails when users prioritize efficiency over engagement. Excessive storytelling creates cognitive friction that directly conflicts with professional workflows.

**When Plain, Direct UI Wins:**

1. **Enterprise Tools**: Data-heavy applications prioritize accuracy over narrative. [NN/G's research on narrative biases](https://www.nngroup.com/articles/narrative-biases/) shows that compelling stories can actually obscure factual analysis—stakeholders need transparent data, not engaging narratives that risk distorting conclusions.

2. **Power Users Skip Onboarding**: [NN/G's video on onboarding](https://www.nngroup.com/videos/onboarding-skip-it-when-possible/) emphasizes that experienced users want "Skip" options. [Research across 200+ onboarding flows](https://designerup.co/blog/i-studied-the-ux-ui-of-over-200-onboarding-flows-heres-everything-i-learned) shows narrative-heavy tutorials create mental load that expert users actively avoid.

3. **Functional vs. Narrative Balance**: [Functional design research](https://builtin.com/design-ux/functional-design-strategies) shows top-performing sites blend narrative with utility—but narrative should serve function, not dominate it. The real tension isn't narrative vs. functional; it's [aesthetics vs. functionality](https://medium.com/@tylerameylegault/functionality-first-aesthetics-second-4071e5d629eb).

**Minimum Viable Narrative:**

- [Enterprise UX design](https://www.koruux.com/blog/master-enterprise-ux-design/) succeeds through minimalism: strip non-essentials, reduce cognitive load, maintain consistency.
- Narrative works best as lightweight context ([user narratives in design](https://uxmag.com/articles/designing-around-the-whole-story-with-user-narratives)) describing workflow, not decorative storytelling.
- [Over-designed UX](https://www.smashingmagazine.com/2022/04/use-storytelling-ux/) fails when narrative creates "too rigid paths" forcing users into predetermined journeys.

**Key Insight**: Narrative should enable task completion, never impede it. For professional users solving real problems, directness beats delight.

## Agent 72: Modern Conversion Copywriting Frameworks Report

*Source: ab57593ed9447a3b0.output*

I'll search for modern conversion copywriting frameworks and research methodologies.
## Modern Conversion Copywriting Frameworks Report

**Contemporary copywriters** blend three research-driven approaches:

### 1. Voice-of-Customer (VoC) Mining
[Copyhackers' methodology](https://copyhackers.com/conversion-copywriting-defined/) mines customer language directly from reviews, support chats, Reddit, YouTube comments, and surveys—avoiding jargon in favor of [exact customer phrasing](https://conversioncopyco.com/voice-of-customer-copywriting-research-overview/). Conversion copywriters report 70% more qualified leads after rewriting with customer voice. [Joanna Wiebe emphasizes research as the most significant part](https://copyhackers.com/about-joanna-wiebe-copywriter/) of the entire process.

### 2. Classic Frameworks, Modernized
- **PAS (Problem-Agitate-Solve)**: Opens with customer pain, intensifies emotional urgency, delivers solution. [Highly effective on short landing pages](https://universaldigitalservices.com/copywriting-formulas-aida-pas-convert/).
- **AIDA (Attention-Interest-Desire-Action)**: Still foundational for capturing interest and building desire.
- **Advanced frameworks** like AICPBSAWN address credibility, proof, and objections—better for [cold traffic on long-form pages](https://thrivethemes.com/copywriting-formulas/).

### 3. Jobs-to-be-Done (JTBD)
Rather than personas, [JTBD focuses on the emotional jobs customers "hire" products to do](https://copyhackers.com/2014/11/jobs-to-be-done-copywriting/). [Customer interviews reveal the exact feeling and need driving purchase decisions](https://www.invespcro.com/blog/jobs-to-be-done-framework-in-conversion-optimization-projects/), eliminating anxiety through mirror-like copy that reflects customer struggle.

### 2026 Practice
Modern copywriters triangulate research sources, extract recurring language themes, then map customer language onto proven frameworks. [Copyhackers' "Seven Sweeps"](https://copyhackers.com/about-joanna-wiebe-copywriter/) provides structured editing discipline. The shift from generic benefit statements to specific, researched customer language is the primary differentiator.

**Key insight**: Copy that converts starts with listening, not writing.

## Agent 73: UX Writing Toolkit - Complete 2026

*Source: ab85f1cdff190419a.output*

I'll search for comprehensive UX writing best practices and patterns to build your toolkit.
## UX Writing Toolkit - Complete 2026

**Core Formulas:**

- **Error Messages**: Problem + Solution path (not blame). Example: "Email required — add one above" vs "Error 400"
- **Empty States**: Positive title + why empty + single strong CTA. Example: "No tasks yet. Start by adding one" not "You have no tasks"
- **Button Labels**: Action verb + outcome (1-3 words, sentence case). Example: "Save draft" vs "Submit"
- **Onboarding**: Welcome message + 3-5 max steps + clear verbs (active voice). Example: "Your file is ready" vs "has been downloaded"
- **Microcopy**: Human, clear, motivating—before/during/after actions (tooltips, hints, success messages)

**Anti-Patterns to Avoid:**
- Vague labels ("Click here," "Yes/No")
- Technical jargon in user-facing messages
- Generic error messages without solutions
- Overly long empty states or onboarding tours (80% skip if >5 steps)
- Passive voice or fear-based language

**Testing:** A/B test copy variations (HubSpot saw 17% lift changing "Start free trial" to "Get started free")

**Key Sources:**
- [UX Writing Best Practices 2026](https://www.designstudiouiux.com/blog/ux-writing-best-practices/)
- [Microcopy Patterns](https://www.microcopy.me/)
- [Error Message Copywriting](https://www.sketch.com/blog/how-to-write-user-friendly-error-messages/)
- [Empty States](https://www.uxpin.com/studio/blog/ux-best-practices-designing-the-overlooked-empty-states/)
- [Button Labels](https://medium.com/uxdworld/8-best-practices-to-write-useful-buttons-labels-5b047db8349f)
- [Onboarding Patterns](https://www.chameleon.io/blog/onboarding-ux-patterns)

## Agent 74: Narrative & CRO: Conversion Optimization Report

*Source: aba761f820477ecc7.output*

I'll search for the intersection of narrative and conversion rate optimization to find concrete insights on this topic.
## Narrative & CRO: Conversion Optimization Report

**Key Finding:** Narrative is a high-impact CRO lever, but *copy elements* (headlines, CTAs, value props) drive measurable lift through A/B testing more frequently than broader story structure.

### Most Testable Narrative Elements
1. **Headlines** - Highest visibility, 30%+ conversion lift observed
2. **Value proposition placement** - Determines whether users continue reading
3. **Tone/voice style** - Formal vs. conversational vs. narrative vs. inspirational
4. **Narrative framing** - Personal story vs. feature/benefit lists (documented 4x lift: 2% to 8%)
5. **CTA messaging** - Decision-point copy has measurable impact

### What A/B Tests Reveal
- **Story structure vs. individual copy:** Specific copy changes outperform broad narrative rewrites in measurable tests
- **Emotional connection drives retention:** Storytelling creates emotional resonance that increases memorability (users remember stories 5-10x better than facts)
- **Narrative synergy:** Headlines + value prop + CTA tone create compounding narrative effect; 14-30% lifts possible when story structure supports copy
- **Testing methodology matters:** Change one narrative element at a time; multivariate narrative tests dilute attribution

### Narrative vs. Copy Impact
**Narrative wins on:** Trust, brand humanization, memorability, emotional motivation through the decision journey
**Copy wins on:** Testability, measurability, rapid iteration, specific conversion metrics

**Bottom line:** Narrative is the *structure*; copy is the *optimization layer*. Narrative-first strategy establishes emotional context; copy-level A/B testing proves what words convert. Combined: narrative as foundation + copy iteration = highest lift.

### Sources
- [Importance of Storytelling in CRO](https://abmatic.ai/blog/importance-of-storytelling-in-conversion-rate-optimization)
- [Role of Storytelling in CRO](https://abmatic.ai/blog/role-of-storytelling-in-conversion-rate-optimization)
- [Using Storytelling to Enhance Conversions](https://cro.media/insights/seo/storytelling-enhance-conversions-cro/)
- [A/B Tests and Copy Guide](https://medium.com/booking-writes/a-b-tests-and-copy-what-why-how-8cc4ae17eae2)

## Agent 75: Cialdini's 7 Principles of Persuasion + Pre-Suasion for Web

*Source: ac4b06a77f166a153.output*

I'll search for Cialdini's 7 principles of persuasion and pre-suasion as they apply to web design and copy.
## Cialdini's 7 Principles of Persuasion + Pre-Suasion for Web

**The 7 Core Principles:**

1. **Reciprocity** - Free value triggers obligation. Web patterns: free trials, downloadable guides, discounts upfront.

2. **Commitment & Consistency** - People honor small initial agreements. Patterns: email opt-ins, checkboxes, "add to cart" micro-commitments.

3. **Social Proof** - Others' behavior validates ours. Patterns: testimonials with photos/names/titles, star ratings, "bestseller" badges, live purchase counters, user counts ("1M+ users").

4. **Authority** - Experts persuade. Patterns: trust badges (certifications, awards), expert author bios, credentials display, case studies with metrics.

5. **Liking** - Similarity and rapport increase influence. Patterns: customer success stories with relatable profiles, lifestyle imagery, conversational copy tone.

6. **Scarcity** - Limited supply drives urgency. Patterns: "Only 3 left in stock," countdown timers, "early bird pricing," seat limits.

7. **Unity** - Shared identity binds. Patterns: "People like you," community language, shared values messaging, in-group references.

**Pre-Suasion (Critical Context):** The moment *before* persuasion shapes receptivity. Visual priming (imagery, colors, background elements) prepares the mind. Web example: furniture retailer tested cloud backgrounds (trust, openness) vs. penny backgrounds (value-consciousness), directly influencing purchase behavior.

**Key Design Pattern:** Testimonials placed mid-journey (not scattered) with specific results, photos, professions, and objection-countering content outperform generic praise.

---

**Sources:**
- [CXL: Cialdini's Principles](https://cxl.com/blog/cialdinis-principles-persuasion/)
- [Gust de Backer: Cialdini Principles](https://gustdebacker.com/cialdini-principles/)
- [Sue Behavioural Design: All 7 Explained](https://www.suebehaviouraldesign.com/en/blog/cialdini-principles-of-persuasion/)
- [Mindtools: Pre-Suasion](https://www.mindtools.com/ac5miqv/pre-suasion/)
- [Cognitigence: Deep Dive](https://www.cognitigence.com/blog/cialdini-7-principles-of-persuasion)

## Agent 76: Typography as Narrative Tool in Web Design: Research Report

*Source: ac93cab06e65fc3a8.output*

I'll search for comprehensive information on typography as a narrative tool in web design.
## Typography as Narrative Tool in Web Design: Research Report

**Type Hierarchy as Information Architecture**
Type hierarchy directly serves as information architecture, organizing content from general to specific. Sequential structures with clear typographic differentiation create compelling narratives that guide users through content flow. Fonts function as visual markers that communicate urgency, importance, and emotional weight—subconscious cues shaping user perception before conscious reading occurs.

**Font Personality and Brand Voice Alignment**
Each typeface carries psychological weight: serifs signal trust and sophistication (formal voice), while sans-serifs convey modernity and honesty (forward-thinking voice). Font psychology operates subconsciously, triggering emotional responses instantly. Consistent typographic choices strengthen credibility; misaligned selections confuse and weaken messaging. Typographic personality directly reinforces or undermines brand narrative, making font selection a strategic storytelling decision.

**Variable Fonts as Dynamic Narrative Tools**
Variable fonts represent evolution in typographic storytelling—adapting weight, width, and optical sizing across contexts. This flexibility allows brands to shift tone as narratives unfold, creating responsive type systems that enhance emotional specificity. Rather than static letterforms, variable fonts enable "character evolution" within stories, with typography transforming alongside narrative development.

**Type Choices as Narrative Reinforcement**
Typography reinforces narrative through mood-setting, attention guidance, and emotional resonance. Well-chosen fonts strengthen visual narratives; poor selections undermine them entirely. Modern design treats typography as a primary design voice—using extreme weights, custom letterforms, and experimental kerning as visual language elements, not mere text vessels.

---

- [Typography as Storytelling: Crafting Narratives](https://webcraftingcode.com/design-fundamentals/typography-as-storytelling-crafting-narratives-with-text-in-web-design/)

- [Font Psychology in Web Design](https://www.mockplus.com/blog/post/font-psychology)

## Mission 25 — OWASP Updates

**Findings:**

The OWASP Top 10 was updated in late 2024/early 2025, confirmed as the 2025 edition. Key changes from the 2021 version:

| Rank | 2025 Category | Change vs 2021 |
|------|---------------|----------------|
| A01 | Broken Access Control | Unchanged; SSRF rolled in |
| A02 | Security Misconfiguration | Up from #5 |
| A03 | Software Supply Chain Failures | Expanded from "Vulnerable & Outdated Components" |
| A04 | Cryptographic Failures | Down from #2 |
| A05 | Injection | Down from #3 |
| A06 | Insecure Design | Down from #4 |
| A07 | Authentication Failures | Unchanged, renamed |
| A08 | Software or Data Integrity Failures | NEW |
| A09 | Logging & Alerting Failures | — |
| A10 | Mishandling of Exceptional Conditions | NEW |

The **OWASP API Security Top 10** has NOT been updated since 2023. The 2023 list remains the current authoritative API-specific reference. No 2025/2026 API edition has been released.

A separate **OWASP Top 10 for LLM Applications 2025** exists (published November 2024). Prompt Injection holds #1 for the second edition. System Prompt Leakage is a newly added entry.

The API Security list (2023) should be the reference for any API audit skill.

## Mission 26 — AI-Specific Security Threats

**Findings:**

Three significant frameworks have emerged since late 2024:

**ASTRIDE** (December 2024, arXiv:2512.04785): A threat modeling platform specifically for agentic AI. Extends the classic STRIDE model with a new "A" category covering AI Agent-Specific Attacks. Uses vision-language models to analyze data flow diagrams automatically. Identifies: prompt injection, context poisoning, unsafe tool invocation, reasoning subversion, and opaque agent-to-agent communication as primary vectors.

**OWASP LLM Top 10 2025** key entries relevant to web-god:
1. Prompt Injection (LLM01) — #1 for two consecutive editions; OWASP now classifies this alongside SQLi in severity
2. System Prompt Leakage (new) — extraction of internal rules, permissions, and decision logic
3. Memory Poisoning — persistent corruption of RAG/long-term memory stores
4. Unsafe Code Execution — agents manipulated into executing malicious generated code

**OWASP Agentic Skills Top 10** (released December 2025, a separate dedicated project): Specifically addresses the skill/plugin ecosystem. Covers: Agent Goal Hijacking via poisoned documents, Unsafe Code Execution, Memory Poisoning. The OWASP Foundation notes "no comprehensive security framework for agent skills existed before this project." Skill file injection is explicitly addressed.

**OWASP Top 10 for Agentic Applications 2026** (also December 2025): Covers autonomous agent risks with 100+ contributors. Top risks: prompt injection, tool misuse, data leakage.

**Regulatory pressure:** EU AI Act full enforcement hits August 2, 2026 with fines up to €35M or 7% global revenue. Prompt injection and adversarial robustness are explicitly named for high-risk classifications.

**Sources:**
- [ASTRIDE paper — arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/2512.04785)
- [OWASP LLM Top 10 — Prompt Injection](https://genai.owasp.org/llmrisk/llm01-prompt-injection/)
- [OWASP Agentic Skills Top 10](https://owasp.org/www-project-agentic-skills-top-10/)
- [OWASP Top 10 for Agentic Applications 2026](https://genai.owasp.org/resource/owasp-top-10-for-agentic-applications-for-2026/)
- [OWASP GenAI Agentic Security Release](https://genai.owasp.org/2025/12/09/owasp-genai-security-project-releases-top-10-risks-and-mitigations-for-agentic-ai-security/)
- [LLM Security Risks 2026 — Sombrainc](https://sombrainc.com/blog/llm-security-risks-2026)
- [MITRE ATLAS Framework 2026](https://www.practical-devsecops.com/mitre-atlas-framework-guide-securing-ai-systems/)

**Relevance to web-god:** The web-god package itself is an agentic AI system. The Sentinel agent must be updated to audit its own skill files against the OWASP Agentic Skills Top 10. The skill file format is a real attack surface: a malicious skill file could redirect agent goals, inject tool calls, or exfiltrate context. The ASTRIDE "A" category threats (prompt injection, context poisoning, unsafe tool use) should be a dedicated section in the security agent's playbook.

**Action:** Add an AI/Agentic Security module to the Sentinel agent covering the OWASP Agentic Skills Top 10 and ASTRIDE's AI-specific threat categories. Implement skill file validation (schema enforcement, source verification). Add prompt injection as a P0 audit item for any LLM-facing code. Reference EU AI Act compliance checklist for any production deployments. **Priority: P0, Effort: L**

## Mission 27 — GitHub Actions Security

**Findings:**

GitHub published an explicit 2026 Actions Security Roadmap (January 2026) directly in response to a wave of supply chain attacks (tj-actions/changed-files, Nx, trivy-action compromises in early 2026).

**Key 2026 roadmap items:**

1. **Dependency Locking**: A new `dependencies:` section in workflow YAML that locks all direct and transitive action dependencies to commit SHAs, analogous to `go.sum`. This closes the tag-mutable attack vector that enabled the tj-actions incident.

2. **Centralized Policy Enforcement**: Workflow execution protections built on GitHub's ruleset framework — moving from per-workflow configuration to org-wide enforceable policy, improving auditability.

3. **Egress Controls**: Enterprise-grade network egress restrictions for workflows to prevent data exfiltration during compromised runs.

**SLSA and Artifact Attestations:**

- GitHub Artifact Attestations (GA as of 2024) provide **SLSA v1.0 Build Level 2** by default.
- Combining with reusable workflows achieves **SLSA v1.0 Build Level 3** (highest practical level): isolated builds, verified source history, strictly controlled provenance.
- Attestations use the in-toto format with Sigstore-issued short-lived signing certificates.
- Available free for public repositories; Enterprise Cloud required for private repos.
- January 2026 GitHub changelog confirmed "code-to-cloud traceability and SLSA Build Level 3 security."

**Supply chain attack pattern:** The 2026 incidents showed attackers compromising third-party action repositories to inject malicious steps into consumer pipelines. Pinning actions to commit SHAs (not tags) is the current best practice and will become enforced with the new dependency locking feature.

**Sources:**
- [GitHub Actions 2026 Security Roadmap — GitHub Blog](https://github.blog/news-insights/product-news/whats-coming-to-our-github-actions-2026-security-roadmap/)
- [SLSA Level 3 with GitHub Actions — GitHub Blog](https://github.blog/security/supply-chain-security/slsa-3-compliance-with-github-actions/)
- [GitHub SLSA Build Level 3 Changelog — Jan 2026](https://github.blog/changelog/2026-01-20-strengthen-your-supply-chain-with-code-to-cloud-traceability-and-slsa-build-level-3-security/)
- [Artifact Attestations — GitHub Docs](https://docs.github.com/en/actions/concepts/security/artifact-attestations/)
- [Artifact Attestations + Reusable Workflows for SLSA Level 3 — GitHub Docs](https://docs.github.com/actions/security-guides/using-artifact-attestations-and-reusable-workflows-to-achieve-slsa-v1-build-level-3)
- [Supply Chain Attacks and the Fix — Medium, March 2026](https://medium.com/@jbpoley/the-security-scanner-turned-spy-github-actions-supply-chain-attacks-and-the-fix-that-works-19ddf3107593)

**Relevance to web-god:** The devops agent / CI-CD skill needs immediate updates. Any workflow templates generated for users must pin actions to commit SHAs, add artifact attestations for SLSA Level 2+, and include `permissions:` blocks scoped minimally. The 2026 supply chain incidents are a direct threat to any project using common third-party actions.

**Action:** Update the devops agent's workflow templates to: (1) pin all `uses:` to commit SHAs, (2) add `actions/attest-build-provenance` for artifacts, (3) add minimal `permissions:` blocks per job, (4) document the path to SLSA Level 3 via reusable workflows. Monitor the dependency-locking feature for GA rollout and adopt it when available. **Priority: P1, Effort: M**

## Mission 28 — CSP Evolution

**Findings:**

**CSP Level 3 Status:** Remains a W3C Working Draft (latest revision: June 6, 2025). It is being actively revised but has not reached Candidate Recommendation. No major new directives were added between 2024 and March 2026 — the spec continues refining existing directives.

**Notable CSP Level 3 changes vs Level 2:**
- `frame-src` un-deprecated (it was deprecated in CSP2, now back as a distinct directive in CSP3)
- `navigate-to` directive was removed from CSP3
- `strict-dynamic` token: allows dynamically loaded scripts to inherit trust from a nonce/hash-trusted parent, without allowlisting hosts
- `require-trusted-types-for 'script'` and `trusted-types` directives added for Trusted Types enforcement

**Trusted Types Browser Support (as of February 2026):**
- **Chrome/Edge (Chromium):** Full support — Trusted Types has been enforced here since Chrome 83 (2020)
- **Firefox:** Mozilla reversed its historical position in late 2023 and committed to implementing Trusted Types. As of February 2026, Firefox support is still "not yet supported" in current stable versions (Firefox 150+), but implementation is actively in progress
- **Safari:** No confirmed implementation timeline. Support remains absent in stable releases
- **Practical status:** Trusted Types cannot yet be enforced universally cross-browser. `require-trusted-types-for` is safe to use with a `Content-Security-Policy-Report-Only` header for monitoring, but enforcing it hard will break Firefox and Safari users

**Recommended modern CSP posture (2026):**
```
Content-Security-Policy:
  default-src 'none';
  script-src 'strict-dynamic' 'nonce-{random}' https:;
  object-src 'none';
  base-uri 'none';
  require-trusted-types-for 'script';   ← enforces in Chrome/Edge only for now
  trusted-types default;
```

**Sources:**
- [CSP Level 3 — W3C Working Draft](https://www.w3.org/TR/CSP3/)
- [CSP MDN Reference](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/Guides/CSP)
- [trusted-types CSP directive — MDN](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/Reference/Headers/Content-Security-Policy/trusted-types)
- [Trusted Types API — MDN](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/Trusted_Types_API)
- [Can I Use — Trusted Types](https://caniuse.com/trusted-types)
- [Mozilla decides Trusted Types is worthy — The Register](https://www.theregister.com/2023/12/21/mozilla_decides_trusted_types_is/)
- [OWASP CSP Cheat Sheet](https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Content_Security_Policy_Cheat_Sheet.html)
- [What's New in CSP v3 — Medium](https://medium.com/@appsecwarrior/whats-new-in-csp-v3-992c44c0425e)

**Relevance to web-god:** The security agent's CSP recommendations need to distinguish between what can be safely enforced today vs. what should be added in report-only mode. Generating `require-trusted-types-for 'script'` in enforcement mode without this caveat will ship broken sites for Firefox/Safari users. The `strict-dynamic` token should replace host allowlists in all template outputs.

**Action:** Update the security agent's CSP template generation to: (1) use `strict-dynamic` + nonce as the default script trust model instead of host allowlists, (2) add `require-trusted-types-for 'script'` in `Content-Security-Policy-Report-Only` by default with a note that enforcement is Chrome/Edge-only until Firefox ships support, (3) remove `navigate-to` if present (removed from CSP3). **Priority: P2, Effort: S**

## 2026 Cinematic Web Design Awards Trends: Research Report

**What's Winning:**
Scroll-driven narratives dominate Awwwards 2026. Scroll storytelling (scrollytelling) transforms page scrolling into choreographed experiences with narrative flow. Motion-triggered animations, multi-directional navigation, and 3D immersive design are signature techniques earning awards.

**New Scroll Techniques:**
Kinetic typography animates text with scroll movement. Modern parallax creates dimensional depth with performance optimization focus. Scroll-triggered animations with reactive elements guide users through content like chapters in a story.

**WebGL/3D/Particle Trends:**
WebGL powers immersive experiences with interactive 3D models and real-time visual effects. Projects like OHZI Interactive (Awwwards Site of the Day) use WebGL for exceptional technical execution with mouse-triggered distortions. Animated abstract 3D forms in glass and metal materials create mood and depth, replacing flat gradients.

**Visual Patterns:**
Oversized typography layered over cinematic hero videos. Immersive VR-like experiences with mixed scroll directions. Interactive 3D constellations and navigable visualizations. Performance-conscious design balancing visual impact with accessibility.

**Impact:** Interactive scrollytelling increases engagement by 85%, e-commerce conversions by 8.4%, and product page conversions up to 40%.

## Agent 79: Layout as Narrative: How Spatial Decisions Tell Stories

*Source: acbce3aac9fc35876.output*

I'll search for information on layout as narrative in web design, exploring how spatial decisions tell stories.
## Layout as Narrative: How Spatial Decisions Tell Stories

**Whitespace as Pause.** Like punctuation in literature, whitespace functions as intentional breathing room. It signals where users should pause, process, and reflect. A line pulled into its own space becomes emphasized; blank space between sections marks a scene break. This negative space "is where feeling lives"—it's not empty but full of meaning, controlling pacing and preventing cognitive overwhelm.

**Density as Intensity.** Visual hierarchy through layout density creates emotional intensity. Tightly packed content conveys urgency or complexity; sparse layouts invite contemplation. Designers manipulate element size, contrast, and placement to guide the eye's journey, making layout a form of cinematic storytelling where the viewer discovers information in intended sequence.

**Grid-Breaking as Disruption.** Bento grids organize content into compartments like chapters, but their power lies in variable sizing. Changing block proportions creates visual roadmaps—larger blocks command attention, disrupting predictability and signaling narrative shifts. Each compartment becomes a "page in a book," weaving visual narratives through deliberate constraint-breaking.

**Full-Bleed as Immersion.** Full-bleed layouts extend content to screen edges, borrowed from publishing's "printed to the edge" technique. This removes distraction, creating immersive editorial experiences where readers get "lost in narrative, not distracted by clutter." Layered grid systems—combining hierarchical and modular structures—guide eyes through rhythm and create spatial flow.

**The Core Insight:** Layout decisions ARE narrative decisions. Manuscript grids support flow; visual hierarchy determines what readers discover first; spacing controls emotional pacing. Modern web design recognizes that how information is spatially organized shapes how it's emotionally received—typography, color, and placement work together to build worlds around content.

---

- [The Power of White Space: IxDF](https://ixdf.org/literature/article/the-power-of-white-space)
- [Whitespace in UX Design: UX Bulletin](https://www.ux-bulletin.com/whitespace-improves-readability-trust-conversions/)

## Mission 5 — Frontend Architecture AI Tools

**Findings:**

The gap between component generation and architecture decisions is real and unaddressed by current tools.

**v0 (Vercel):** Remains frontend-first and component-generation-centric. The February 2026 update added Git integration, VS Code-style editor, and database connectivity, but architecture decisions — performance strategy, component boundary rules, state ownership, routing structure — remain firmly outside v0's scope. v0 generates production React/Next.js/Tailwind/shadcn code using fine-tuned proprietary models, but it does not encode *why* decisions were made. No ADRs, no constraint reasoning, no trade-off capture.

**Cursor 2.0:** Introduced agent-first architecture. Complex decisions are explicitly routed to external frontier models (Claude Opus 4.6, GPT-5.2) for "high-level reasoning to ensure the agent's plan adheres to system-wide invariants." Cursor uses RLVR training — rewarded for verifiable outcomes, not just syntactic correctness. Codebase-wide multi-agent runs (up to 8 simultaneous agents via git worktree isolation) are in production. However, Cursor still does not *encode* decisions — it reasons about them at execution time. A `guidelines.md` / `CLAUDE.md` contract is the expected mechanism for architecture constraints.

**Windsurf (Cascade):** Introduced Plan Mode for smarter task decomposition and side-by-side dual-agent runs. Cascade agents can do automatic project analysis and multi-file coordination with real-time context awareness. Still no dedicated architecture-decision record output format.

**The Gap vs. Component Gen:** None of v0, Cursor, or Windsurf encode architecture decisions as persistent, versioned artifacts. They generate code or reason about decisions ephemerally. The gap is: no tool produces an **ADR** (Architecture Decision Record) as a first-class output, no tool tracks *why* a pattern was chosen over alternatives, and no tool enforces constraints across sessions. This is web-god's Strategist agent's exact job.

**Sources:**
- [Designing high-performance agentic systems (Cursor agent case study)](https://medium.com/@khayyam.h/designing-high-performance-agentic-systems-an-architectural-case-study-of-the-cursor-agent-ab624e4a0a64)
- [Cursor 2.0: Agent-First Architecture Complete Guide](https://www.digitalapplied.com/blog/cursor-2-0-agent-first-architecture-guide)
- [Windsurf Review 2026](https://www.secondtalent.com/resources/windsurf-review/)
- [v0 by Vercel: Complete Guide 2026](https://www.nxcode.io/resources/news/v0-by-vercel-complete-guide-2026)
- [AI-Ready Frontend Architecture Guide — LogRocket](https://blog.logrocket.com/ai-ready-frontend-architecture-guide/)
- [Agentic AI 2026: Autonomous Frontend Architectures](https://bryancode.dev/en/blog/the-rise-of-agentic-ai-building-autonomous-frontend-workflows-in-2026)

**Relevance to web-god:** web-god's `frontend` skill → `frontend-architect` agent → ADR output is the *only* tool in the ecosystem doing this systematically. The `frontend-architect` agent in `/Users/inspectre/Developer/web-god-pkg/agents/frontend/architect.md` (routing decisions, component boundary rules, state ownership) fills the gap that v0/Cursor/Windsurf all leave open.

**Action:** Surface this differentiation explicitly. Add a `compatibility` frontmatter field to web-god skills noting they pair with v0/Cursor/Windsurf for implementation *after* architecture is decided. Consider a `guidelines-md` output artifact from the `frontend-architect` agent so Claude Code / Cursor can consume web-god's ADRs as live context. **Priority: P1, Effort: S**

## Mission 6 — Agent Orchestration Patterns

**Findings:**

Three frameworks dominate in 2026, each with a distinct primary pattern:

**LangGraph — Graph-based workflows with Supervisor pattern:**
The production-dominant choice for complex pipelines. Uses directed acyclic/cyclic graphs with conditional edges and built-in checkpointing with time-travel. The `langgraph-supervisor` library (now available as a standalone package) implements hierarchical multi-agent systems with a `supervisor → workers` topology that mirrors an org chart. Current best practice in 2026 is to use the supervisor pattern via tool-calling (not the library) for maximum context engineering control. Multi-level hierarchies (`supervisor → sub-supervisors → workers`) are production-supported. LangGraph Cloud provides hosted execution with built-in monitoring and LangSmith tracing.

**CrewAI — Role-based crew coordination:**
Models agents as role-playing crew members (`role`, `backstory`, `goal`). Optimized for fast prototyping and production-ready team coordination. Process types: sequential (chain outputs), hierarchical (manager delegates). Teams frequently prototype in CrewAI then migrate to LangGraph for complex state management needs. Best for well-defined task decomposition where roles don't need dynamic adaptation.

**AutoGen / AG2 — Conversational group chat:**
The v0.4 rewrite (now AG2) introduced event-driven core, async-first execution, and pluggable orchestration. `GroupChat` with a `selector` agent determines who speaks next. Best for human-in-the-loop and natural multi-agent conversation. Weaker on deterministic workflow control vs. LangGraph.

**Bleeding-edge patterns (2026):**
- Agents that dynamically spawn sub-agents (not statically defined crew/graph)
- LangGraph Cloud for hosted, observable, scalable agent execution
- Tool-calling supervisors rather than pre-wired graphs (more flexible context control)
- Worktree isolation for parallel agents (validated by Cursor's 8-agent production runs)

**Sources:**
- [Best Multi-Agent Frameworks in 2026](https://gurusup.com/blog/best-multi-agent-frameworks-2026)
- [LangGraph vs CrewAI vs AutoGen 2026 — o-mega.ai](https://o-mega.ai/articles/langgraph-vs-crewai-vs-autogen-top-10-agent-frameworks-2026)
- [Agent Orchestration 2026 — Iterathon](https://iterathon.tech/blog/ai-agent-orchestration-frameworks-2026)
- [LangGraph Supervisor Library](https://changelog.langchain.com/announcements/langgraph-supervisor-a-library-for-hierarchical-multi-agent-systems)
- [LangGraph in 2026 — DEV Community](https://dev.to/ottoaria/langgraph-in-2026-build-multi-agent-ai-systems-that-actually-work-3h5)
- [Multi-Agent Frameworks — adopt.ai](https://www.adopt.ai/blog/multi-agent-frameworks)

**Relevance to web-god:** web-god's orchestration model closely mirrors LangGraph's supervisor pattern (Conductor → domain skills → specialized agents). The skill pipeline tables (e.g., `frontend`: Architect → Component Designer → Builder → Validation) are a sequential hierarchical crew topology. web-god currently does not use dynamic sub-agent spawning or checkpointing — the two bleeding-edge capabilities that distinguish LangGraph's production story from simpler frameworks.

**Action:** Add checkpoint/handover output artifacts to multi-step pipelines (web-god already has a `handover` skill — wire it to pipeline step completions). Explore `context:fork` per pipeline step so each step runs in an isolated subagent with its own context window, matching the LangGraph node isolation pattern. **Priority: P1, Effort: M**

## Mission 7 — Claude Code Skills 2.0 Features

**Findings:**

Claude Code 2.1 introduced several features that web-god's current skills do not use. The full frontmatter field table from the live docs reveals significant gaps:

**Fields web-god DOES use:** `name`, `description`

**Fields web-god does NOT use (but could):**

| Field | What it does | web-god relevance |
|---|---|---|
| `context: fork` | Runs skill in isolated subagent; skill body becomes the prompt | High — pipeline steps should fork |
| `agent` | Which subagent type to use when forked (`Explore`, `Plan`, `general-purpose`, or custom) | High — `frontend-architect` agent should be named here |
| `hooks` | Agent-scoped PreToolUse/PostToolUse/Stop hooks scoped to skill lifecycle | Medium — validation gates |
| `model` | Pin model for this skill (e.g. `opus` for architecture) | High — Conductor/Strategist should use opus |
| `effort` | `low`/`medium`/`high`/`max` — overrides session effort level | Medium — scrollytelling pipeline could use `max` |
| `disable-model-invocation` | Prevents auto-triggering; must be user-invoked | High — `deploy`, `devops` skills should have this |
| `user-invocable: false` | Hides from `/` menu; background knowledge only | Medium — reference-only skills |
| `argument-hint` | Autocomplete hint shown for skill args (`[url] [format]`) | Low — UX polish |
| `allowed-tools` | Tools usable without per-use approval when skill is active | Medium — locked-down read-only audit skills |
| `paths` | Glob patterns that gate when skill auto-loads | Medium — `testing` skill loads only when in test files |
| `compatibility` | Environment requirements string | Low-medium — agentskills.io compliance |

**Dynamic context injection (`!` backtick syntax):** Shell commands embedded in skill content run *before* Claude sees the prompt; output is substituted inline. web-god uses none of this. Example: the `performance` skill could inject `!`npm run build:analyze`` output directly before Claude sees the prompt.

**Agent-scoped lifecycle hooks (Claude Code 2.1):** `PreToolUse`, `PostToolUse`, `Stop`, `SubagentStop`, `SessionStart` hooks can be defined in skill frontmatter. They only fire during that skill's lifecycle. web-god has 3 git hooks but no skill-level hooks.

**`context: fork` + named `agent`:** Running a skill in a forked context with a named custom agent (e.g., web-god's `frontend-architect`) is the canonical pattern for pipeline steps. web-god's skills currently read as inline instruction fragments — converting them to `context: fork` with named agents would match the documented best practice and give each step a clean context window.

**Sources:**
- [Claude Code Skills Docs — code.claude.com](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/skills) (live fetch above)
- [Claude Code 2.1: Pain Points Fixed](https://paddo.dev/blog/claude-code-21-pain-points-addressed/)
- [Agent Skills Fork — Rick Hightower](https://medium.com/@richardhightower/from-approval-hell-to-just-do-it-how-agent-skills-fork-governed-sub-agents-in-claude-code-2-1-c0438416433a)
- [Claude Code Skills 2.0 — Towards AI](https://medium.com/@richardhightower/claude-code-agent-skills-2-0-from-custom-instructions-to-programmable-agents-ab6e4563c176)
- [Build Agent Skills Faster with Claude Code 2.1](https://medium.com/@richardhightower/build-agent-skills-faster-with-claude-code-2-1-release-6d821d5b8179)

**Relevance to web-god:** web-god is using approximately 2 of ~14 available frontmatter fields. The biggest functional gaps are `context: fork`, `model`, `disable-model-invocation`, and `hooks`. These aren't cosmetic — `context: fork` changes execution isolation, `model` enforces the routing rules already defined in `/Users/inspectre/.claude/rules/common/performance.md`, and `disable-model-invocation` prevents Claude from auto-firing destructive skills like `devops`.

**Action:** Upgrade all 9 skill frontmatter blocks. Minimum changes: add `disable-model-invocation: true` to `devops` and `security` (side-effects), add `model: opus` to `frontend`, `backend`, and `scrollytelling` (orchestration), add `context: fork` to pipeline-step skills, add `compatibility` field to all for agentskills.io compliance. **Priority: P0, Effort: S**

## Mission 8 — agentskills.io Open Standard

**Findings:**

The official spec (fetched live from agentskills.io/specification) defines the following:

**Required fields:** `name`, `description`
**Optional fields:** `license`, `compatibility`, `metadata`, `allowed-tools`

**Name constraints:** 1-64 chars, lowercase alphanumeric + hyphens only, no leading/trailing/consecutive hyphens, must match parent directory name.

**Directory structure standard:**
```
skill-name/
├── SKILL.md          # Required
├── scripts/          # Optional: executable code
├── references/       # Optional: documentation
├── assets/           # Optional: templates, resources
```

**Progressive disclosure model:** metadata (~100 tokens loaded at startup), instructions (<5000 tokens when activated), resources (on-demand). Recommended max 500 lines for SKILL.md body.

**web-god compliance assessment:**

| Check | web-god status |
|---|---|
| `name` field present | PASS — all 9 skills have it |
| `description` field present | PASS — all 9 skills have it |
| `name` matches directory name | PASS — `frontend/SKILL.md` has `name: frontend`, etc. |
| Name format (lowercase + hyphens only) | PASS |
| `license` field | FAIL — missing from all 9 skills |
| `compatibility` field | FAIL — missing from all 9 skills |
| `metadata` field (author, version) | FAIL — missing from all 9 skills |
| `references/` directory | PASS — all 9 skills have `references/` with principles docs |
| `scripts/` directory | PARTIAL — not present in any skill (web-god uses inline Bash, not bundled scripts) |
| `assets/` directory | FAIL — not used |
| SKILL.md body under 500 lines | needs verification |
| File references linked from SKILL.md | PARTIAL — principles docs exist but are not all referenced from SKILL.md body |

**Claude Code extensions beyond the standard** (not in agentskills.io spec): `context`, `agent`, `model`, `effort`, `hooks`, `paths`, `shell`, `disable-model-invocation`, `user-invocable`, `argument-hint`, `$ARGUMENTS` substitution, `!`command`` dynamic injection. These are Claude Code-specific and not part of the open standard — important for portability considerations.

**Validator tool:** `skills-ref validate ./my-skill` (from `github.com/agentskills/agentskills`) can check compliance programmatically.

**Sources:**
- [agentskills.io/specification](https://agentskills.io/specification) (live fetch above)
- [GitHub: agentskills/agentskills](https://github.com/agentskills/agentskills)
- [Agent Skills — Simon Willison](https://simonwillison.net/2025/Dec/19/agent-skills/)
- [Agent Skills overview — Anthropic](https://platform.claude.com/docs/en/agents-and-tools/agent-skills/overview)
- [SKILL.md Specification — DeepWiki](https://deepwiki.com/agentskills/agentskills/2.2-skill.md-specification)
- [Agent Skills Guide 2026 — Serenities AI](https://serenitiesai.com/articles/agent-skills-guide-2026)

**Relevance to web-god:** web-god passes the two hard requirements (name + description). It gets partial credit for `references/` directories. It fails on `license`, `compatibility`, and `metadata`. These are not functional gaps — they are **ecosystem/portability gaps**. Without `license` and `compatibility`, web-god skills cannot be published to any skill registry or shared with other Claude Code users in a spec-compliant way. Without `metadata.version`, there is no version tracking when skills are updated.

**Action:** Add the three missing optional fields to all 9 SKILL.md frontmatter blocks. Suggested values: `license: MIT`, `compatibility: Requires Claude Code with web-god plugin installed`, `metadata: { author: web-god, version: "1.0" }`. ## Agent 82: No-Code Scrollytelling Ceiling (March 2026)

*Source: ad1946bc0c4723b33.output*

I'll search for current no-code scrollytelling capabilities in 2026.
## No-Code Scrollytelling Ceiling (March 2026)

**Current Capabilities:**
No-code platforms now deliver impressive scroll effects. Webflow and Framer both offer native scroll animations with parallax, fade-on-scroll, and spring-physics transforms. Readymag adds horizontal animations while maintaining vertical scroll. Vev and Shorthand focus on data storytelling with drag-and-drop interactivity.

**Ceiling:**
- Fixed UI paradigm (elements move, not scroll behavior)
- Limited to preset animation curves (spring physics standardized across platforms)
- Single-axis focus (vertical dominates; horizontal scroll requires workarounds)
- Integration gaps (CMS data + animations require custom code)
- Performance ceiling on mobile (complex parallax still laggy)

**Web-God Differentiation:**
Code-first approach unlocks: (1) **Custom scroll behaviors** (horizontal carousels, fixed sticky-release patterns), (2) **Data-driven animation** (real-time scroll position → chart updates), (3) **Micro-interaction sequencing** (orchestrate 10+ elements with sub-100ms timing), (4) **Performance optimization** (GPU-accelerated transforms, throttled scroll listeners), (5) **Narrative control** (scroll direction detection, pause/resume states).

**Key Insight:** No-code excels at *simple reveal patterns*; web-god owns *scrollytelling as architecture* (scroll as narrative medium, not just trigger).

---

- [Framer Scroll Effects](https://www.framer.com/blog/scroll-effects/)
- [Vev Scrollytelling](https://www.vev.design/scrollytelling/)
- [How to Implement Scrollytelling (6 libraries)](https://pudding.cool/process/how-to-implement-scrollytelling/)

## Agent 83: Emotional Design in Web Narrative: Research Report

*Source: ad19e9265f3f63b18.output*

I'll search for information on emotional design in web narratives using WebSearch.
## Emotional Design in Web Narrative: Research Report

### Norman's Three Levels of Emotional Processing

Don Norman's framework defines emotional design through three interconnected layers:

- **Visceral**: Automatic, perceptual response to appearance—how colors, typography, and visual elements make users feel instantly.
- **Behavioral**: Conscious interaction with usability and function—how smoothly the product works builds confidence.
- **Reflective**: Meaning-making layer—how cultural context and sustained use create emotional connection over time.

All three must work together for effective emotional design.

### Plutchik's Emotion Wheel: A Design Palette

Robert Plutchik's 8-primary-emotion model (joy, trust, fear, surprise, sadness, anticipation, anger, disgust) provides designers with an "emotional color palette." Primary emotions blend to create secondary ones—joy + anticipation = optimism. Designers deliberately use this mapping to elicit specific user responses and drive both loyalty and action.

### Jungian Brand Archetypes

Carl Jung's 12 archetypes (Hero, Explorer, Lover, Creator, Sage, Caregiver, Everyman, Innocent, Magician, Jester, Ruler, Outlaw) shape how brands emotionally resonate. Nike embodies the Hero with bold typography and dynamic layouts; Explorers use dynamic discovery-oriented design. Archetypes appear consistently across visual design, messaging, tone, and product—creating cohesive emotional narratives.

### 2026 Trend: Emotion-Driven Design

2026 marks a deliberate shift toward emotional design after years of minimalism. Designers use storytelling, organic layouts, and nostalgia as intentional tools—not excess, but precision. When users feel curiosity, joy, or intrigue, they spend longer, remember more, and develop deeper brand connection.

**Key Strategy**: Map your brand to a Jungian archetype → apply Norman's three levels across the user journey → use Plutchik's wheel to select and blend specific emotional triggers.

### Sources
- [Norman's Three Levels of Design | IxDF](https://www.interaction-design.org/literature/article/norman-s-three-levels-of-design)
- [Plutchik's Wheel of Emotions | IxDF](https://ixdf.org/literature/topics/wheel-of-emotions)
- [12 Brand Archetypes by Carl Jung | Visme](https://visme.co/blog/brand-archetypes/)
- [Why 2026 Is the Year of Emotion-Driven UX | Slinky Web Design](https://www.slinkywebdesign.com.au/why-2026-is-the-year-of-emotion-driven-ux)
