## Mission 35 — Scroll-Driven Data Visualization

**Findings:**

Scrollytelling is mainstream and technically maturing fast in 2026:

1. **The Pudding (2026)**: Still the gold standard. Recent pieces include 145 years of Congressional "democracy" mentions as a scroll narrative, music band success odds via progressive data disclosure, and colorism in Vogue fashion. The Pudding's work is the benchmark for grammar and storytelling density.

2. **NYT Interactive**: Remains the canonical reference (Derek Jeter's 342,000 swings piece still cited). NYT continues leading investigative scroll narratives.

3. **CSS scroll-triggered animations (Chrome 145, Feb 2026)**: The new `animation-trigger` CSS property fires time-based animations when crossing a scroll offset — a native replacement for IntersectionObserver-based JavaScript. This means scroll-reveal data visualizations can run entirely in CSS with compositor-thread performance.

4. **CSS scroll-state queries (Chrome 133+)**: `container-type: scroll-state` lets CSS detect when an element is stuck, snapped, or overflowing — no JavaScript. Game-changer for sticky axis labels in data visualizations.

5. **Spiral scrollytelling with `sibling-index()`**: CSS-Tricks demonstrated full spiral text scroll effects using pure CSS `sibling-index()` — signals a new era of CSS-native complex scrollytelling without GSAP.

6. **Maglr's 2026 best-of list**: B2B software, health, real estate are adopting scrollytelling — it's no longer journalism-only. Immersive content is winning attention wars.

## Mission 36 — WebGPU for Scroll Effects

**Findings:**

WebGPU crossed the production threshold in early 2026:

1. **Browser support (Jan 2026 milestone)**: Firefox 147 shipped WebGPU on Jan 13, 2026. Safari 26 ships it on macOS Tahoe 26, iOS 26, iPadOS 26, and visionOS 26. Chrome/Edge have supported it since v113. Combined: ~70% global coverage with WebGL 2 fallback for the remaining ~30% (primarily Linux).

2. **Three.js r171 (Sept 2025) — production-ready**: `import * as THREE from 'three/webgpu'` gives WebGPU rendering with automatic WebGL 2 fallback. Zero config. 65% of new web 3D projects are already using it. Only caveat: initialization is async.

3. **Performance vs WebGL**:
   - CPU frame time roughly halved vs WebGL in equivalent scenes
   - Draw-call-heavy scenes: 15,000 objects at 15 FPS (WebGL) → 200,000 objects at 60 FPS (WebGPU)
   - Compute shaders: 10–100x gains for particles and physics
   - Simple scenes with few draw calls: minimal to no gain
   - For scroll effects specifically: multi-layered parallax particle systems and compute-driven distortion effects are now feasible at 60 FPS on midrange hardware

4. **The nuance — not universally faster**: On simple scenes WebGPU can be slower due to async pipeline compilation overhead. The win is specifically for complex, draw-call-heavy, or compute-heavy scroll effects (particle fields, fluid distortion, instanced geometry).

5. **TSL (Three Shading Language)**: Three.js r171 introduced TSL — a JavaScript-based shader language that compiles to both WGSL (WebGPU) and GLSL (WebGL). Write shaders once, run everywhere.

**Sources:**
- [What's New in Three.js 2026: WebGPU — Utsubo](https://www.utsubo.com/blog/threejs-2026-what-changed)
- [WebGPU 2026: 70% Browser Support, 15x Performance Gains — ByteIota](https://byteiota.com/webgpu-2026-70-browser-support-15x-performance-gains/)
- [WebGPU Hits Critical Mass — WebGPU.com](https://www.webgpu.com/news/webgpu-hits-critical-mass-all-major-browsers/)
- [WebGPU Three.js Migration Guide 2026 — Utsubo](https://www.utsubo.com/blog/webgpu-threejs-migration-guide)
- [WebGL vs WebGPU: The Performance Gap — Medium, Jan 2026](https://gjgalante.medium.com/webgl-vs-webgpu-the-performance-gap-fbd121fb221a)
- [WebGPU and WebNN: Browser AI APIs — ddevtools, Jan 2026](https://www.ddevtools.com/updates/2026-01-webgpu-webnn-browser-ai)
- [WebGPU vs WebGL: Why 2026 Browsers Can Render Console-Quality Games — CybermaXia](https://cybermaxia.com/en/blog/webgpu-vs-webgl-browser-2026-render-game-konsol)
- [WebGPU Renderer — Three.js Docs](https://threejs.org/docs/pages/WebGPURenderer.html)
- [WebGPU is Supported by All Major Browsers — VideoCardz](https://videocardz.com/newz/webgpu-is-now-supported-by-all-major-browsers)
- [Three.js WebGPU + TSL — WebGPU & Threlte](https://threlte.xyz/docs/learn/advanced/webgpu)

**Relevance to web-god:** WebGPU is the new default for any 3D scroll effect in web-god. `import * as THREE from 'three/webgpu'` with automatic WebGL 2 fallback means zero compatibility cost. TSL means shader code written for web-god's 3D scroll templates compiles to both targets. The performance ceiling for scroll-driven particle systems, fluid distortion, and instanced geometry has risen dramatically.

**Action:** Update web-god's 3D scroll templates to use `three/webgpu` import and async renderer init. Add TSL-based shader examples for scroll-driven distortion effects. Document the "complex scenes only" performance caveat so the choreographer agent selects WebGPU paths appropriately. Priority: **P1**, Effort: **S**

## Agent 105: Motion Design as Narrative: Beyond Decoration

*Source: af1ddb212735c39c3.output*

I'll search for research on motion design as narrative to build a comprehensive report.
## Motion Design as Narrative: Beyond Decoration

Animation transcends decoration when it becomes the **voice** of the interface—a communicative layer that guides attention, marks transitions, and shapes how users interpret content.

### Transitions as Punctuation

Transitions function as narrative grammar: a **cut** creates urgency or drama, a **dissolve** signals continuation or passage of time, a **zoom** draws focus to what matters. Shape morphing connects ideas, slow fades suggest finality, quick whips leap to moments of excitement. Motion design has beats, motifs, and crescendos like music—thoughtfully crafted rhythms speak directly to emotions.

[Motion Design and Storytelling: Engaging Your Audience](https://blog.pixelfreestudio.com/motion-design-and-storytelling-engaging-your-audience/) • [Six Essential Motion Design Transitions](https://www.schoolofmotion.com/blog/six-essential-motion-design-transitions-tutorial)

### Entrance Animations as Emphasis

Entrance animations control **when** content appears, directing focus through timing. They introduce elements at precisely the moment they matter narratively—not scattered randomly but sequenced to support the story's rhythm. Every movement serves purpose; animations without meaning distract rather than clarify.

[Articulate Storyline 360: Emphasis Animations](https://blog.iconlogic.com/2024/01/articulate-storyline-360-january-2024-update-includes-library-of-entrance-animations.html)

### When Motion IS the Message

In UX, animation becomes communication—the interface's body language in a conversation with users. Loading animations reassure through movement. State changes morph icons to signal mode transitions (pencil → disk = Edit → Save). Interactive feedback creates dialogue: instant reactions strengthen user-system connection. Duration matters: 200-500ms feels natural; linear motion feels mechanical.

[The Role of Animation in UX – NN/G](https://www.nngroup.com/articles/animation-purpose-ux/) • [Motion That Makes Sense](https://www.concretecms.com/about/blog/web-design/using-animation-to-improve-ux) • [User Experience Animation: Enhancing UX](https://educationalvoice.co.uk/user-experience-animation/)

**Core principle**: Motion succeeds when it reveals meaning, not when it decorates it.

## AI Copywriting Tools Landscape 2026: Research Report

### Market Overview
The AI copywriting space has matured into specialized platforms with sophisticated brand voice and audience awareness capabilities. Leading tools like [Jasper AI](https://www.jasper.ai/), [Copy.ai](https://www.copy.ai/), [Writesonic](https://www.writesonic.com/), and [Anyword](https://anyword.com/) now function as multi-assistant systems rather than simple text generators.

### Brand Voice & Consistency
Top tools employ three core approaches:
1. **Content Training**: Tools like [Copy.ai's Brand Voice](https://www.copy.ai/features/brand-voice) and [Typeface](https://www.typeface.ai/) analyze existing content samples to capture tone, terminology, and style.
2. **Manual Definition**: [Jasper](https://www.jasper.ai/use-cases/copywriting) allows custom brand voice profiles with multiple author-specific variants.
3. **Channel-Specific Voices**: Advanced platforms support different voices per platform/audience segment.

### Audience Awareness & Narrative
Emerging strengths include [Copy.ai's specialized agents](https://www.copy.ai/) for Account-Based Marketing, translation/localization, and audience segment targeting. However, most tools remain template-driven rather than narrative-architecture focused.

### Web-God's Differentiation Opportunity
Most competitors excel at **volume and templates** but lack:
- **Deep narrative structure design** (hero's journey, story arcs)
- **Audience psychology mapping** (values, pain points, motivation triggers)
- **Integrated content architecture** (how copy pieces interconnect across pages)
- **Visual-copywriting cohesion** (design tokens + voice guidelines)

Web-god could own the intersection of **strategic narrative design + scalable brand-consistent copy generation** — positioning it not as a text generator but as a content architecture platform.

- [Best AI Copywriting Tools Compared - Dave Swift](https://daveswift.com/best-ai-copywriting-tools-compared/)

---

## Full Extraction: Psychology of the Interface PDF

### 1. Gestalt Principles Covered

**Pre-attentive attributes driving all Gestalt perception:** color, orientation, size, proximity. Operating window: 200–250ms (subconscious, before foveal reading begins).

**1.1 Proximity** — Primary grouping mechanism. Spatial interval is the strongest available signal of semantic relationship. Overrides similarity in color, shape, and style.
- UI applications: form field grouping (Shipping vs. Billing sections), navigation icon clusters (social share bars create "toolbar" effect without bounding boxes), restaurant-menu-style label-to-item tightening
- Anti-pattern: "ambiguous spacing" — label equidistant between two data points forces eye saccades to verify ownership

**1.2 Similarity** — Groups by shared attribute (color, shape, size, texture, orientation).
- UI applications: affordance signaling (all clickable elements share one visual signature), categorical filtering (sponsored results use distinct background tint for instant segregation)
- Anti-pattern: "Christmas tree" button vocabulary (ghost + filled + text link + FAB = unteachable grammar); "sameness" collapse when everything is too similar
- Goal: distinct "classes" — all primary actions look like X, all secondary like Y

**1.3 Common Region** — Elements inside a closed region (border or distinct background) are perceived as one group. Stronger cue than Proximity in many contexts.
- UI applications: Card UI (Pinterest, Airbnb, Trello — brain perceives card as one object, not five parts), dashboard sectioning (gray sidebar vs. white content area creates Figure-Ground separation)
- Key finding: even loosely spaced elements inside a border are read as unified

**1.4 Closure** — Brain fills in missing information to perceive a complete shape.
- UI applications: horizontal carousel cards clipped at screen edge signal scrollability without a "Next" button; icon design (gear icon, Apple logo) reduces ink without losing recognition
- Benefit: reduces ink-to-data ratio, lighter interfaces

**1.5 Continuity** — Eye follows smoothest path regardless of how lines are actually drawn.
- UI applications: stepper patterns (Cart > Shipping > Payment on horizontal axis creates momentum; vertical/disjointed stacking disrupts flow and feels longer); left-margin alignment creates a "rail" that speeds scanning
- Eye-tracking confirmation: ragged left margins force constant saccade adjustment

**Figure-Ground** — Mentioned in context of Common Region (sidebar vs. content area creates Figure-Ground separation anchoring user focus). Not given its own dedicated section but cited as an emergent effect of Common Region application.

---

### 2. Pre-Attentive Processing

- Window: **200–250 milliseconds** — subconscious accumulation in sensory memory before conscious/foveal attention activates
- Pre-attentive attributes listed: color, orientation, size, proximity
- Function: user "feels" interface is intuitive when structure matches the brain's natural sorting algorithms; contradicting these laws forces System 2 (conscious) thinking, causing friction, fatigue, and higher abandonment

---

### 3. Von Restorff Effect (Isolation Effect)

Named after Hedwig von Restorff (1933 dissertation): isolated item in a homogeneous list is noticed AND remembered better.

**Mechanism:** Brain suppresses neural response to repetitive stimuli (habituation). Deviant stimulus triggers neural spike — immediate attention capture + enhanced memory encoding.

**UI Applications:**
- CTA button design: the primary action must be the single most distinctive element in the viewport
- Color rule: no "magic color" — the effective color is the complementary color to the site's dominant palette. Von Restorff relies on **relative contrast**, not absolute values
  - HubSpot A/B test: red CTA outperformed green by 21% (site was predominantly green)
  - Dropbox counter-example: green outperformed blue by 32% (site was predominantly blue)
- Pricing tables: middle/"Recommended" tier is made larger, differently colored, or given a "Most Popular" ribbon — draws eye and anchors comparison, interacts with Decoy Effect
- Memory effect: users more likely to remember a product highlighted as "Best Value"

**Critical limitation — "Christmas Tree" Effect:**
- Von Restorff is non-scalable; requires uniform background to function
- If everything is highlighted, nothing is highlighted
- Banner Blindness: cluttered visual fields trigger filtering of aggressive interruptions
- Rule: **budget isolation for exactly one primary action per screen**. More than one "primary" CTA = zero effective CTAs

---

### 4. Glanceability Audit Checklist

**This document does not contain a Glanceability Audit Checklist.** The PDF has no such named section, heuristic list, or pass/fail criteria. The "Glanceability Audit" belongs to a different document than the one at the provided path.

---

### 5. 3-Second Rule / Consumption Speed Hierarchy (Glance/Scan/Study Modes)

**This document does not contain these constructs.** No 3-Second Rule, no named Glance Mode / Scan Mode / Study Mode hierarchy appears anywhere in the 18 pages. This content is absent from this PDF.

---

**Not covered in this document.** Tufte is not referenced. The phrase "ink-to-data ratio" appears once in the Closure section ("By reducing the ink-to-data ratio, Closure creates interfaces that feel lighter"), but this is a passing mention only — there is no dedicated treatment of Tufte's data-ink ratio concept.

---

### 7. Specific Numbers and Thresholds (All)

| Threshold | Value | Context |
|---|---|---|
| Pre-attentive window | 200–250ms | Gestalt processing before conscious attention |
| Doherty Threshold | 400ms | Sub-400ms = continuous flow/addiction state; >400ms = attention fragments |
| Context reload cost | >1 second | User must re-load task context when latency exceeds 1s |
| INP "Good" score | <200ms | Google Core Web Vitals interaction responsiveness |
| LCP "Good" score | ≤2.5 seconds | Google Core Web Vitals page load |
| Miller's Law working memory | 7 ± 2 items | Referenced in context of menu design |
| Optimal nav categories | 5–7 | Combined Hick's Law + Miller's Law recommendation |
| Hick's Law constant b | ~0.155s/option | Empirically derived cognitive processing time per option |
| Hick's: 2 options | 0.245s | Low load, simple binary |
| Hick's: 5 options | 0.400s | Moderate load, standard menu |
| Hick's: 10 options | 0.536s | High load, needs grouping |
| Hick's: 50 options | 0.879s | Cognitive overload, requires search |
| HubSpot CTA lift | +21% | Red vs. green button (dominant-green site) |
| Dropbox CTA lift | +32% | Green vs. blue button (dominant-blue site) |

---

### Practitioner Rules (from Recommendations section)

1. **Audit for Grouping:** Blur-eye "Squint Test" — does Gestalt grouping hold without reading text?
2. **Budget Your Isolation:** Maximum one primary CTA per view. More than one = none.
3. **Count the Choices:** Per menu/form, ask "Can I reduce n? If not, can progressive disclosure reduce visible n at any moment?"
4. **Measure Perceived Latency:** Measure time until UI *updates*, not just server response. If process >1 second, use optimistic UI or shimmer animation skeletons.

## Agent 110: Handley-Clark Content Frameworks: Operational Reference

*Source: bkrjw4ndb.output*

The PDF is 18 pages and I have all of it. Here is the complete extraction.

---

## Handley-Clark Content Frameworks: Operational Reference

### 1. Handley's Complete Framework

**Formula of Three (Utility + Inspiration + Empathy)**
All three must coexist or content fails. Utility alone is dry. Inspiration alone is fluff. Without empathy, it's company-centric noise.

**Pathological Empathy Loop (4 stages, cyclic)**
1. Inhabit the Habitat — visit customers in their natural, vulnerable context (not a focus group lab)
2. Swap Shoes — erase corporate ego; think only in reader's stress, vocabulary, and physical environment
3. Ugly First Draft (TUFD) — "show up and throw up," generate without judgment, bypass the internal censor
4. The Empathy Edit — revise not for grammar but for the reader's clarity; "rework the horse, not polish the saddle"

**So What? Filter**
Apply iteratively to every paragraph. If the answer is still about the company, ask again. Stop only when the answer is entirely about the customer's life.

**Squawk Test**
Cover the logo. Would a competitor's content be indistinguishable? If yes, the voice has failed. Four rules to pass it:
- Define three personality adjectives with "glance" clarifiers (e.g., "Smart" = respects reader intelligence, not pedantic)
- Ditch corporate cartilage: ban "leverage," "synergy," "best-in-class"
- Use "you" and "we," use contractions — informality increases trust, not reduces authority
- Vary sentence length deliberately; rhythm is part of voice

**Rules of Economy**
- No ten-dollar words when one-dollar words work: "help" not "facilitate," "use" not "utilize"
- Max 3 sentences or 6 lines per paragraph
- Insert a subhead every 300 words
- "Lede" (first sentence) and "Kicker" (last sentence) get special attention — the lede hooks, the kicker resolves or calls to action
- "No one will ever complain that you've made things too simple to understand"

---

### 2. Clark's Complete Framework

**Media Authority Model (5-step flywheel)**
Creation → Signal (backlinks, shares) → Traffic → Audience (email list) → Authority. Advertising rents attention; Authority owns it.

**Teaching as Selling**
Reframe sales as education. Teaching establishes the teacher-student trust dynamic. Give away the "how" (method) to sell the "what" (product/service). Operationalized through Cornerstone Content — comprehensive definitive guides on core topics that serve as audience entry points.

**Rule of One**
Every piece of content must have:
- One Reader (write to a single avatar, not a crowd)
- One Big Idea (compelling and surprising; covering multiple ideas dilutes impact)
- One Offer/Promise (multiple choices cause analysis paralysis)

**4 A's Content Structure**
1. Attention — Magnetic Headline (spend 50% of writing time here); formulas: "How to [X] Without [Pain]," "The [Number] Secrets to [Result]," "Do You Recognize the [Number] Early Warning Signs of [Problem]?"
2. Attraction — address specific pain points so the right reader self-selects ("This is for me")
3. Authority — prove expertise by solving a small problem; "show, don't tell"
4. Action — single, clear, logical CTA; if the first three are done, Action is a natural next step, not pressure

**5-Step Strategy Process**
Define ideal customer → Map funnel formats → Generate unique ideas (identify pain, analyze standard advice, offer a better solution) → Create a content calendar → Integrate SEO/services.

---

### 3. Operational Rules for a Copywriting AI Agent

**Word choice**
- Replace: facilitate→help, utilize→use, leverage→use/build, synergy→[delete], best-in-class→[delete]
- Always prefer the shorter word
- Use second-person ("you," "we") over third-person ("the customer," "the company")
- Use contractions

**Headlines**
- Formulas: "How to [X] Without [Y]" / "[Number] Secrets to [X]" / "Do You Recognize [Number] Signs of [Problem]?" / "The [Number] [Adjective] Ways to [X]"
- Headline gets 50% of total writing time
- Clark stat: 8/10 read the headline; only 2/10 read the body — the headline is the ad for the content

**Voice test (Squawk)**
- Strip the logo mentally; if any competitor could have written it, rewrite
- Every brand needs 3 adjectives + clarifiers before writing

**Formatting rules**
- Paragraphs: max 3 sentences / 6 lines
- Subheads: every 300 words, benefit-oriented (not label-oriented)
- Bullets for complex breakdowns
- Mix short punchy sentences with longer flowing ones

**Conversion rules (Rule of One)**
- One reader, one idea, one offer per piece
- Never offer multiple CTAs — pick one

---

### 4. Web Section Mapping

| Page | Handley Principle | Clark Principle | Combined Rule |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Homepage** | Pathological Empathy — lead with their problem, not your product | 4 A's: Attention → Attraction | Open with reader's pain; one promise; one CTA |
| **Blog Post** | TUFD → Empathy Edit; strong lede + kicker; Squawk-passing voice | Magnetic Headline (50% time); 4 A's structure; Rule of One | Headline formula → empathetic lede → teach the "how" → single CTA kicker |
| **Newsletter** | "Focus on the letter not the news"; Personal Lede (analog story) → Pivot → Value → Voice; fortnightly quality > frequency | Benefit-driven subject line; Contextual Hook; The Meat (step-by-step); Soft Pitch | Open with personal human story (Handley), deliver educational meat (Clark), close with soft pitch |
| **About Page** | "Best About Pages are about who you are in relation to your reader" — start with their problem ("You are here because...") | "Talk about yourself only in context of how you serve readers"; include social proof and CTA | Hook (reader's problem) → Hero Story (you as guide, not hero) → Squawk section (personality) → Social Proof → Email CTA |

**Critical synthesis insight:** In the AI era, the Squawk Test is the survival metric. AI can replicate utility and information (Clark's "news") but cannot replicate the Personal Lede, unique perspective, and human habitat-derived empathy (Handley's "letter"). Future-proof content leans into opinion, personal narrative, and proprietary perspective — the value proposition shifts from "we know the facts" to "we have a unique view of the facts."

---
